2035	Me your perfections would not bless;
2036	I am not worthy them in aught;
2037	And honestly 'tis my belief
2038	Our union would produce but grief.
2039	Though now my love might be intense,
2040	Habit would bring indifference.
2041	I see you weep. Those tears of yours
2042	Tend not my heart to mitigate,
2043	But merely to exasperate;
2044	Judge then what roses would be ours,
2045	What pleasures Hymen would prepare
2046	For us, may be for many a year.
2047	"What can be drearier than the house,
2048	Wherein the miserable wife
2049	Deplores a most unworthy spouse
2050	And leads a solitary life?
2051	The tiresome man, her value knowing,
2052	Yet curses on his fate bestowing,
2053	Is full of frigid jealousy,
2054	Mute, solemn, frowning gloomily.
2055	Such am I. This did ye expect,
2056	When in simplicity ye wrote
2057	Your innocent and charming note
2058	With so much warmth and intellect?
2059	Hath fate apportioned unto thee
2060	This lot in life with stern decree?"Ideas and time ne'er backward move;
2061	My soul I cannot renovate--
2062	I love you with a brother's love,
2063	Perchance one more affectionate.
2064	Listen to me without disdain.
2065	A maid hath oft, may yet again
2066	Replace the visions fancy drew;
2067	Thus trees in spring their leaves renew
2068	As in their turn the seasons roll.
2069	'Tis evidently Heaven's will
2070	You fall in love again. But still--
2071	Learn to possess more self-control.
2072	Not all will like myself proceed--
2073	And thoughtlessness to woe might lead."Thus did our friend Oneguine preach:
2074	Tattiana, dim with tears her eyes,
2075	Attentive listened to his speech,
2076	All breathless and without replies.
2077	His arm he offers. Mute and sad,
2078	Tattiana doth accept his aid;
2079	And, hanging down her head, the maid
2080	Around the garden homeward hies.
2081	Together they returned, nor word
2082	Of censure for the same incurred;
2083	The country hath its liberties
2084	And privileges nice allowed,
2085	Even as Moscow, city proud.Confess, O ye who this peruse,
2086	Oneguine acted very well
2087	By poor Tattiana in the blues;
2088	'Twas not the first time, I can tell
2089	You, he a noble mind disclosed,
2090	Though some men, evilly disposed,
2091	Spared him not their asperities.
2092	His friends and also enemies
2093	Esteemed him much as the world goes.
2094	Yes! every one must have his foes,
2095	But Lord! from friends deliver me!
2096	The deuce take friends, my friends, amends
2097	I've had to make for having friends!But how? Quite so. Though I dismiss
2098	Dark, unavailing reverie,
2099	I just hint, in parenthesis,
2100	There is no stupid calumny
2101	Born of a babbler in a loft
2102	And by the world repeated oft,
2103	There is no fishmarket retort
2104	And no ridiculous report,
2105	Which your true friend with a sweet smile
2106	Where fashionable circles meet
2107	A hundred times will not repeat,
2108	Quite inadvertently meanwhile;
2109	And yet he in your cause would strive
2110	And loves you as--a relative!Ahem! Ahem! My reader noble,
2111	Are all your relatives quite well?
2112	Permit me; is it worth the trouble
2113	For your instruction here to tell
2114	What I by relatives conceive?
2115	These are your relatives, believe:
2116	Those whom we ought to love, caress,
2117	With spiritual tenderness;
2118	Whom, as the custom is of men,
2119	We visit about Christmas Day,
2120	Or by a card our homage pay,
2121	That until Christmas comes again
2122	They may forget that we exist.
2123	And so--God bless them, if He list.In this the love of the fair sex
2124	Beats that of friends and relatives:
2125	In love, although its tempests vex,
2126	Our liberty at least survives:
2127	Agreed! but then the whirl of fashion,
2128	The natural fickleness of passion,
2129	The torrent of opinion,
2130	And the fair sex as light as down!
2131	Besides the hobbies of a spouse
2132	Should be respected throughout life
2133	By every proper-minded wife,
2134	And this the faithful one allows,
2135	When in as instant she is lost,--
2136	Satan will jest, and at love's cost.Oh! where bestow our love? Whom trust?
2137	Where is he who doth not deceive?
2138	Who words and actions will adjust
2139	To standards in which we believe?
2140	Oh! who is not calumnious?
2141	Who labours hard to humour us?
2142	To whom are our misfortunes grief
2143	And who is not a tiresome thief?
2144	My venerated reader, oh!
2145	Cease the pursuit of shadows vain,
2146	Spare yourself unavailing pain
2147	And all your love on self bestow;
2148	A worthy object 'tis, and well
2149	I know there's none more amiable.But from the interview what flowed?
2150	Alas! It is not hard to guess.
2151	The insensate fire of love still glowed
2152	Nor discontinued to distress
2153	A spirit which for sorrow yearned.
2154	Tattiana more than ever burned
2155	With hopeless passion: from her bed
2156	Sweet slumber winged its way and fled.
2157	Her health, life's sweetness and its bloom,
2158	Her smile and maidenly repose,
2159	All vanished as an echo goes.
2160	Across her youth a shade had come,
2161	As when the tempest's veil is drawn
2162	Across the smiling face of dawn.Alas! Tattiana fades away,
2163	Grows pale and sinks, but nothing says;
2164	Listless is she the livelong day
2165	Nor interest in aught betrays.
2166	Shaking with serious air the head,
2167	In whispers low the neighbours said:
2168	'Tis time she to the altar went!
2169	But enough! Now, 'tis my intent
2170	The imagination to enliven
2171	With love which happiness extends;
2172	Against my inclination, friends,
2173	By sympathy I have been driven.
2174	Forgive me! Such the love I bear
2175	My heroine, Tattiana dear.Vladimir, hourly more a slave
2176	To youthful Olga's beauty bright,
2177	Into delicious bondage gave
2178	His ardent soul with full delight.
2179	Always together, eventide
2180	Found them in darkness side by side,
2181	At morn, hand clasped in hand, they rove
2182	Around the meadow and the grove.
2183	And what resulted? Drunk with love,
2184	But with confused and bashful air,
2185	Lenski at intervals would dare,
2186	If Olga smilingly approve,
2187	Dally with a dishevelled tress
2188	Or kiss the border of her dress.To Olga frequently he would
2189	Some nice instructive novel read,
2190	Whose author nature understood
2191	Better than Chateaubriand did
2192	Yet sometimes pages two or three
2193	(Nonsense and pure absurdity,
2194	For maiden's hearing deemed unfit),
2195	He somewhat blushing would omit:
2196	Far from the rest the pair would creep
2197	And  they
2198	A game of chess would often play,
2199	Buried in meditation deep,
2200	Till absently Vladimir took
2201	With his own pawn alas! his rook!Homeward returning, he at home
2202	Is occupied with Olga fair,
2203	An album, fly-leaf of the tome,
2204	He leisurely adorns for her.
2205	Landscapes thereon he would design,
2206	A tombstone, Aphrodite's shrine,
2207	Or, with a pen and colours fit,
2208	A dove which on a lyre doth sit;
2209	The "in memoriam" pages sought,
2210	Where many another hand had signed
2211	A tender couplet he combined,
2212	A register of fleeting thought,
2213	A flimsy trace of musings past
2214	Which might for many ages last.Surely ye all have overhauled
2215	A country damsel's album trim,
2216	Which all her darling friends have scrawled
2217	From first to last page to the rim.
2218	Behold! orthography despising,
2219	Metreless verses recognizing
2220	By friendship how they were abused,
2221	Hewn, hacked, and otherwise ill-used.
2222	Upon the opening page ye find:
2223	_Qu'ecrirer-vouz sur ces tablettes?_
2224	Subscribed, _toujours a vous, Annette;_
2225	And on the last one, underlined:
2226	_Who in thy love finds more delight
2227	Beyond this may attempt to write_.Infallibly you there will find
2228	Two hearts, a torch, of flowers a wreath,
2229	And vows will probably be signed:
2230	_Affectionately yours till death_.
2231	Some army poet therein may
2232	Have smuggled his flagitious lay.
2233	In such an album with delight
2234	I would, my friends, inscriptions write,
2235	Because I should be sure, meanwhile,
2236	My verses, kindly meant, would earn
2237	Delighted glances in return;
2238	That afterwards with evil smile
2239	They would not solemnly debate
2240	If cleverly or not I prate.But, O ye tomes without compare,
2241	Which from the devil's bookcase start,
2242	Albums magnificent which scare
2243	The fashionable rhymester's heart!
2244	Yea! although rendered beauteous
2245	By Tolstoy's pencil marvellous,
2246	Though Baratynski verses penned,
2247	The thunderbolt on you descend!
2248	Whene'er a brilliant courtly dame
2249	Presents her quarto amiably,
2250	Despair and anger seize on me,
2251	And a malicious epigram
2252	Trembles upon my lips from spite,--
2253	And madrigals I'm asked to write!
2254	But Lenski madrigals ne'er wrote
2255	In Olga's album, youthful maid,
2256	To purest love he tuned his note
2257	Nor frigid adulation paid.
2258	What never was remarked or heard
2259	Of Olga he in song averred;
2260	His elegies, which plenteous streamed,
2261	Both natural and truthful seemed.
2262	Thus thou, Yazykoff, dost arise
2263	In amorous flights when so inspired,
2264	Singing God knows what maid admired,
2265	And all thy precious elegies,
2266	Sometime collected, shall relate
2267	The story of thy life and fate.
2268	Since Fame and Freedom he adored,
2269	Incited by his stormy Muse
2270	Odes Lenski also had outpoured,
2271	But Olga would not such peruse.
2272	When poets lachrymose recite
2273	Beneath the eyes of ladies bright
2274	Their own productions, some insist
2275	No greater pleasure can exist
2276	Just so! that modest swain is blest
2277	Who reads his visionary theme
2278	To the fair object of his dream,
2279	A beauty languidly at rest,
2280	Yes, happy--though she at his side
2281	By other thoughts be occupied.But I the products of my Muse,
2282	Consisting of harmonious lays,
2283	To my old nurse alone peruse,
2284	Companion of my childhood's days.
2285	Or, after dinner's dull repast,
2286	I by the button-hole seize fast
2287	My neighbour, who by chance drew near,
2288	And breathe a drama in his ear.
2289	Or else ,
2290	Exhausted by my woes and rhymes,
2291	I sail upon my lake at times
2292	And terrify a swarm of ducks,
2293	Who, heard the music of my lay,
2294	Take to their wings and fly away.But to Oneguine! _A propos!_
2295	Friends, I must your indulgence pray.
2296	His daily occupations, lo!
2297	Minutely I will now portray.
2298	A hermit's life Oneguine led,
2299	At seven in summer rose from bed,
2300	And clad in airy costume took
2301	His course unto the running brook.
2302	There, aping Gulnare's bard, he spanned
2303	His Hellespont from bank to bank,
2304	And then a cup of coffee drank,
2305	Some wretched journal in his hand;
2306	Then dressed himself...
2307	Sound sleep, books, walking, were his bliss,
2308	The murmuring brook, the woodland shade,
2309	The uncontaminated kiss
2310	Of a young dark-eyed country maid,
2311	A fiery, yet well-broken horse,
2312	A dinner, whimsical each course,
2313	A bottle of a vintage white
2314	And solitude and calm delight.
2315	Such was Oneguine's sainted life,
2316	And such unconsciously he led,
2317	Nor marked how summer's prime had fled
2318	In aimless ease and far from strife,
2319	The curse of commonplace delight.
2320	And town and friends forgotten quite.This northern summer of our own,
2321	On winters of the south a skit,
2322	Glimmers and dies. This is well known,
2323	Though we will not acknowledge it.
2324	Already Autumn chilled the sky,
2325	The tiny sun shone less on high
2326	And shorter had the days become.
2327	The forests in mysterious gloom
2328	Were stripped with melancholy sound,
2329	Upon the earth a mist did lie
2330	And many a caravan on high
2331	Of clamorous geese flew southward bound.
2332	A weary season was at hand--
2333	November at the gate did stand.The morn arises foggy, cold,
2334	The silent fields no peasant nears,
2335	The wolf upon the highways bold
2336	With his ferocious mate appears.
2337	Detecting him the passing horse
2338	Snorts, and his rider bends his course
2339	And wisely gallops to the hill.
2340	No more at dawn the shepherd will
2341	Drive out the cattle from their shed,
2342	Nor at the hour of noon with sound
2343	Of horn in circle call them round.
2344	Singing inside her hut the maid
2345	Spins, whilst the friend of wintry night,
2346	The pine-torch, by her crackles bright.Already crisp hoar frosts impose
2347	O'er all a sheet of silvery dust
2348	(Readers expect the rhyme of _rose_,
2349	There! take it quickly, if ye must).
2350	Behold! than polished floor more nice
2351	The shining river clothed in ice;
2352	A joyous troop of little boys
2353	Engrave the ice with strident noise.
2354	A heavy goose on scarlet feet,
2355	Thinking to float upon the stream,
2356	Descends the bank with care extreme,
2357	But staggers, slips, and falls. We greet
2358	The first bright wreathing storm of snow
2359	Which falls in starry flakes below.How in the country pass this time?
2360	Walking? The landscape tires the eye
2361	In winter by its blank and dim
2362	And naked uniformity.
2363	On horseback gallop o'er the steppe!
2364	Your steed, though rough-shod, cannot keep
2365	His footing on the treacherous rime
2366	And may fall headlong any time.
2367	Alone beneath your rooftree stay
2368	And read De Pradt or Walter Scott!
2369	Keep your accounts! You'd rather not?
2370	Then get mad drunk or wroth; the day
2371	Will pass; the same to-morrow try--
2372	You'll spend your winter famously!
2373	A true Childe Harold my Eugene
2374	To idle musing was a prey;
2375	At morn an icy bath within
2376	He sat, and then the livelong day,
2377	Alone within his habitation
2378	And buried deep in meditation,
2379	He round the billiard-table stalked,
2380	The balls impelled, the blunt cue chalked;
2381	When evening o'er the landscape looms,
2382	Billiards abandoned, cue forgot,
2383	A table to the fire is brought,
2384	And he waits dinner. Lenski comes,
2385	Driving abreast three horses gray.
2386	"Bring dinner now without delay!"Upon the table in a trice
2387	Of widow Clicquot or Moet
2388	A blessed bottle, placed in ice,
2389	For the young poet they display.
2390	Like Hippocrene it scatters light,
2391	Its ebullition foaming white
2392	My heart of old would captivate.
2393	The last poor obol I was worth--
2394	Was it not so?--for thee I gave,
2395	And thy inebriating wave
2396	Full many a foolish prank brought forth;
2397	And oh! what verses, what delights,
2398	Delicious visions, jests and fights!Alas! my stomach it betrays
2399	With its exhilarating flow,
2400	And I confess that now-a-days
2401	I prefer sensible Bordeaux.
2402	To cope with Ay no more I dare,
2403	For Ay is like a mistress fair,
2404	Seductive, animated, bright,
2405	But wilful, frivolous, and light.
2406	But thou, Bordeaux, art like the friend
2407	Who in the agony of grief
2408	Is ever ready with relief,
2409	Assistance ever will extend,
2410	Or quietly partake our woe.
2411	All hail! my good old friend Bordeaux!The fire sinks low. An ashy cloak
2412	The golden ember now enshrines,
2413	And barely visible the smoke
2414	Upward in a thin stream inclines.
2415	But little warmth the fireplace lends,
2416	Tobacco smoke the flue ascends,
2417	The goblet still is bubbling bright--
2418	Outside descend the mists of night.
2419	How pleasantly the evening jogs
2420	When o'er a glass with friends we prate
2421	Just at the hour we designate
2422	The time between the wolf and dogs--
2423	I cannot tell on what pretence--
2424	But lo! the friends to chat commence."How are our neighbours fair, pray tell,
2425	Tattiana, saucy Olga thine?"--
2426	"The family are all quite well--
2427	Give me just half a glass of wine--
2428	They sent their compliments--but oh!
2429	How charming Olga's shoulders grow!
2430	Her figure perfect grows with time!
2431	She is an angel! We sometime
2432	Must visit them. Come! you must own,
2433	My friend, 'tis but to pay a debt,
2434	For twice you came to them and yet
2435	You never since your nose have shown.
2436	But stay! A dolt am I who speak!
2437	They have invited you this week.""Me?"--"Yes! It is Tattiana's fete
2438	Next Saturday. The Larina
2439	Told me to ask you. Ere that date
2440	Make up your mind to go there."--"Ah!
2441	It will be by a mob beset
2442	Of every sort and every set!"--
2443	"Not in the least, assured am I!"--
2444	"Who will be there?"--"The family.
2445	Do me a favour and appear.
2446	Will you?"--"Agreed."--"I thank you, friend,"
2447	And saying this Vladimir drained
2448	His cup unto his maiden dear.
2449	Then touching Olga they depart
2450	In fresh discourse. Such, love, thou art!He was most gay. The happy date
2451	In three weeks would arrive for them;
2452	The secrets of the marriage state
2453	And love's delicious diadem
2454	With rapturous longing he awaits,
2455	Nor in his dreams anticipates
2456	Hymen's embarrassments, distress,
2457	And freezing fits of weariness.
2458	Though we, of Hymen foes, meanwhile,
2459	In life domestic see a string
2460	Of pictures painful harrowing,
2461	A novel in Lafontaine's style,
2462	My wretched Lenski's fate I mourn,
2463	He seemed for matrimony born.He was beloved: or say at least,
2464	He thought so, and existence charmed.
2465	The credulous indeed are blest,
2466	And he who, jealousy disarmed,
2467	In sensual sweets his soul doth steep
2468	As drunken tramps at nightfall sleep,
2469	Or, parable more flattering,
2470	As butterflies to blossoms cling.
2471	But wretched who anticipates,
2472	Whose brain no fond illusions daze,
2473	Who every gesture, every phrase
2474	In true interpretation hates:
2475	Whose heart experience icy made
2476	And yet oblivion forbade.
2477	The Fete
2478	'Oh, do not dream these fearful dreams,
2479	O my Svetlana.'--Joukovski
2480	That year the autumn season late
2481	Kept lingering on as loath to go,
2482	All Nature winter seemed to await,
2483	Till January fell no snow--
2484	The third at night. Tattiana wakes
2485	Betimes, and sees, when morning breaks,
2486	Park, garden, palings, yard below
2487	And roofs near morn blanched o'er with snow;
2488	Upon the windows tracery,
2489	The trees in silvery array,
2490	Down in the courtyard magpies gay,
2491	And the far mountains daintily
2492	O'erspread with Winter's carpet bright,
2493	All so distinct, and all so white!
2494	Winter! The peasant blithely goes
2495	To labour in his sledge forgot,
2496	His pony sniffing the fresh snows
2497	Just manages a feeble trot
2498	Though deep he sinks into the drift;
2499	Forth the _kibitka_ gallops swift,
2500	Its driver seated on the rim
2501	In scarlet sash and sheepskin trim;
2502	Yonder the household lad doth run,
2503	Placed in a sledge his terrier black,
2504	Himself transformed into a hack;
2505	To freeze his finger hath begun,
2506	He laughs, although it aches from cold,
2507	His mother from the door doth scold.
2508	In scenes like these it may be though,
2509	Ye feel but little interest,
2510	They are all natural and low,
2511	Are not with elegance impressed.
2512	Another bard with art divine
2513	Hath pictured in his gorgeous line
2514	The first appearance of the snows
2515	And all the joys which Winter knows.
2516	He will delight you, I am sure,
2517	When he in ardent verse portrays
2518	Secret excursions made in sleighs;
2519	But competition I abjure
2520	Either with him or thee in song,
2521	Bard of the Finnish maiden young.
2522	Tattiana, Russian to the core,
2523	Herself not knowing well the reason,
2524	The Russian winter did adore
2525	And the cold beauties of the season:
2526	On sunny days the glistening rime,
2527	Sledging, the snows, which at the time
2528	Of sunset glow with rosy light,
2529	The misty evenings ere Twelfth Night.
2530	These evenings as in days of old
2531	The Larinas would celebrate,
2532	The servants used to congregate
2533	And the young ladies fortunes told,
2534	And every year distributed
2535	Journeys and warriors to wed.
2536	Tattiana in traditions old
2537	Believed, the people's wisdom weird,
2538	In dreams and what the moon foretold
2539	And what she from the cards inferred.
2540	Omens inspired her soul with fear,
2541	Mysteriously all objects near
2542	A hidden meaning could impart,
2543	Presentiments oppressed her heart.
2544	Lo! the prim cat upon the stove
2545	With one paw strokes her face and purrs,
2546	Tattiana certainly infers
2547	That guests approach: and when above
2548	The new moon's crescent slim she spied,
2549	Suddenly to the left hand side,
2550	She trembled and grew deadly pale.
2551	Or a swift meteor, may be,
2552	Across the gloom of heaven would sail
2553	And disappear in space; then she
2554	Would haste in agitation dire
2555	To mutter her concealed desire
2556	Ere the bright messenger had set.
2557	When in her walks abroad she met
2558	A friar black approaching near,
2559	Or a swift hare from mead to mead
2560	Had run across her path at speed,
2561	Wholly beside herself with fear,
2562	Anticipating woe she pined,
2563	Certain misfortune near opined.
2564	Wherefore? She found a secret joy
2565	In horror for itself alone,
2566	Thus Nature doth our souls alloy,
2567	Thus her perversity hath shown.
2568	Twelfth Night approaches. Merry eves!
2569	When thoughtless youth whom nothing grieves,
2570	Before whose inexperienced sight
2571	Life lies extended, vast and bright,
2572	To peer into the future tries.
2573	Old age through spectacles too peers,
2574	Although the destined coffin nears,
2575	Having lost all in life we prize.
2576	It matters not. Hope e'en to these
2577	With childlike lisp will lie to please.
2578	Tattiana gazed with curious eye
2579	On melted wax in water poured;
2580	The clue unto some mystery
2581	She deemed its outline might afford.
2582	Rings from a dish of water full
2583	In order due the maidens pull;
2584	But when Tattiana's hand had ta'en
2585	A ring she heard the ancient strain:
2586	_The peasants there are rich as kings,
2587	They shovel silver with a spade,
2588	He whom we sing to shall be made
2589	Happy and glorious_. But this brings
2590	With sad refrain misfortune near.
2591	Girls the _kashourka_ much prefer.
2592	Frosty the night; the heavens shone;
2593	The wondrous host of heavenly spheres
2594	Sailed silently in unison--
2595	Tattiana in the yard appears
2596	In a half-open dressing-gown
2597	And bends her mirror on the moon,
2598	But trembling on the mirror dark
2599	The sad moon only could remark.
2600	List! the snow crunches--he draws nigh!
2601	The girl on tiptoe forward bounds
2602	And her voice sweeter than the sounds
2603	Of clarinet or flute doth cry:
2604	"What is your name?" The boor looked dazed,
2605	And "Agathon" replied, amazed.
2606	Tattiana
2607	By night prepared for sorcery,
2608	And in the bathroom did command
2609	To lay two covers secretly.
2610	But sudden fear assailed Tattiana,
2611	And I, remembering Svetlana,
2612	Become alarmed. So never mind!
2613	I'm not for witchcraft now inclined.
2614	So she her silken sash unlaced,
2615	Undressed herself and went to bed
2616	And soon Lel hovered o'er her head.
2617	Beneath her downy pillow placed,
2618	A little virgin mirror peeps.
2619	'Tis silent all. Tattiana sleeps.
2620	A dreadful sleep Tattiana sleeps.
2621	She dreamt she journeyed o'er a field
2622	All covered up with snow in heaps,
2623	By melancholy fogs concealed.
2624	Amid the snowdrifts which surround
2625	A stream, by winter's ice unbound,
2626	Impetuously clove its way
2627	With boiling torrent dark and gray;
2628	Two poles together glued by ice,
2629	A fragile bridge and insecure,
2630	Spanned the unbridled torrent o'er;
2631	Beside the thundering abyss
2632	Tattiana in despair unfeigned
2633	Rooted unto the spot remained.As if against obstruction sore
2634	Tattiana o'er the stream complained;
2635	To help her to the other shore
2636	No one appeared to lend a hand.
2637	But suddenly a snowdrift stirs,
2638	And what from its recess appears?
2639	A bristly bear of monstrous size!
2640	He roars, and "Ah!" Tattiana cries.
2641	He offers her his murderous paw;
2642	She nerves herself from her alarm
2643	And leans upon the monster's arm,
2644	With footsteps tremulous with awe
2645	Passes the torrent But alack!
2646	Bruin is marching at her back!She, to turn back her eyes afraid,
2647	Accelerates her hasty pace,
2648	But cannot anyhow evade
2649	Her shaggy myrmidon in chase.
2650	The bear rolls on with many a grunt:
2651	A forest now she sees in front
2652	With fir-trees standing motionless
2653	In melancholy loveliness,
2654	Their branches by the snow bowed down.
2655	Through aspens, limes and birches bare,
2656	The shining orbs of night appear;
2657	There is no path; the storm hath strewn
2658	Both bush and brake, ravine and steep,
2659	And all in snow is buried deep.The wood she enters--bear behind,--
2660	In snow she sinks up to the knee;
2661	Now a long branch itself entwined
2662	Around her neck, now violently
2663	Away her golden earrings tore;
2664	Now the sweet little shoes she wore,
2665	Grown clammy, stick fast in the snow;
2666	Her handkerchief she loses now;
2667	No time to pick it up! afraid,
2668	She hears the bear behind her press,
2669	Nor dares the skirting of her dress
2670	For shame lift up the modest maid.
2671	She runs, the bear upon her trail,
2672	Until her powers of running fail.She sank upon the snow. But Bruin
2673	Adroitly seized and carried her;
2674	Submissive as if in a swoon,
2675	She cannot draw a breath or stir.
2676	He dragged her by a forest road
2677	Till amid trees a hovel showed,
2678	By barren snow heaped up and bound,
2679	A tangled wilderness around.
2680	Bright blazed the window of the place,
2681	Within resounded shriek and shout:
2682	"My chum lives here," Bruin grunts out.
2683	"Warm yourself here a little space!"
2684	Straight for the entrance then he made
2685	And her upon the threshold laid.Recovering, Tania gazes round;
2686	Bear gone--she at the threshold placed;
2687	Inside clink glasses, cries resound
2688	As if it were some funeral feast.
2689	But deeming all this nonsense pure,
2690	She peeped through a chink of the door.
2691	What doth she see? Around the board
2692	Sit many monstrous shapes abhorred.
2693	A canine face with horns thereon,
2694	Another with cock's head appeared,
2695	Here an old witch with hirsute beard,
2696	There an imperious skeleton;
2697	A dwarf adorned with tail, again
2698	A shape half cat and half a crane.Yet ghastlier, yet more wonderful,
2699	A crab upon a spider rides,
2700	Perched on a goose's neck a skull
2701	In scarlet cap revolving glides.
2702	A windmill too a jig performs
2703	And wildly waves its arms and storms;
2704	Barking, songs, whistling, laughter coarse,
2705	The speech of man and tramp of horse.
2706	But wide Tattiana oped her eyes
2707	When in that company she saw
2708	Him who inspired both love and awe,
2709	The hero we immortalize.
2710	Oneguine sat the table by
2711	And viewed the door with cunning eye.All bustle when he makes a sign:
2712	He drinks, all drink and loudly call;
2713	He smiles, in laughter all combine;
2714	He knits his brows--'tis silent all.
2715	He there is master--that is plain;
2716	Tattiana courage doth regain
2717	And grown more curious by far
2718	Just placed the entrance door ajar.
2719	The wind rose instantly, blew out
2720	The fire of the nocturnal lights;
2721	A trouble fell upon the sprites;
2722	Oneguine lightning glances shot;
2723	Furious he from the table rose;
2724	All arise. To the door he goes.Terror assails her. Hastily
2725	Tattiana would attempt to fly,
2726	She cannot--then impatiently
2727	She strains her throat to force a cry--
2728	She cannot--Eugene oped the door
2729	And the young girl appeared before
2730	Those hellish phantoms. Peals arise
2731	Of frantic laughter, and all eyes
2732	And hoofs and crooked snouts and paws,
2733	Tails which a bushy tuft adorns,
2734	Whiskers and bloody tongues and horns,
2735	Sharp rows of tushes, bony claws,
2736	Are turned upon her. All combine
2737	In one great shout: she's mine! she's mine!"Mine!" cried Eugene with savage tone.
2738	The troop of apparitions fled,
2739	And in the frosty night alone
2740	Remained with him the youthful maid.
2741	With tranquil air Oneguine leads
2742	Tattiana to a corner, bids
2743	Her on a shaky bench sit down;
2744	His head sinks slowly, rests upon
2745	Her shoulder--Olga swiftly came--
2746	And Lenski followed--a light broke--
2747	His fist Oneguine fiercely shook
2748	And gazed around with eyes of flame;
2749	The unbidden guests he roughly chides--
2750	Tattiana motionless abides.The strife grew furious and Eugene
2751	Grasped a long knife and instantly
2752	Struck Lenski dead--across the scene
2753	Dark shadows thicken--a dread cry
2754	Was uttered, and the cabin shook--
2755	Tattiana terrified awoke.
2756	She gazed around her--it was day.
2757	Lo! through the frozen windows play
2758	Aurora's ruddy rays of light--
2759	The door flew open--Olga came,
2760	More blooming than the Boreal flame
2761	And swifter than the swallow's flight.
2762	"Come," she cried, "sister, tell me e'en
2763	Whom you in slumber may have seen."But she, her sister never heeding,
2764	With book in hand reclined in bed,
2765	Page after page continued reading,
2766	But no reply unto her made.
2767	Although her book did not contain
2768	The bard's enthusiastic strain,
2769	Nor precepts sage nor pictures e'en,
2770	Yet neither Virgil nor Racine
2771	Nor Byron, Walter Scott, nor Seneca,
2772	Nor the _Journal des Modes_, I vouch,
2773	Ever absorbed a maid so much:
2774	Its name, my friends, was Martin Zadeka,
2775	The chief of the Chaldean wise,
2776	Who dreams expound and prophecies.Brought by a pedlar vagabond
2777	Unto their solitude one day,
2778	This monument of thought profound
2779	Tattiana purchased with a stray
2780	Tome of "Malvina," and but three
2781	And a half rubles down gave she;
2782	Also, to equalise the scales,
2783	She got a book of nursery tales,
2784	A grammar, likewise Petriads two,
2785	Marmontel also, tome the third;
2786	Tattiana every day conferred
2787	With Martin Zadeka. In woe
2788	She consolation thence obtained--
2789	Inseparable they remained.
2790	The dream left terror in its train.
2791	Not knowing its interpretation,
2792	Tania the meaning would obtain
2793	Of such a dread hallucination.
2794	Tattiana to the index flies
2795	And alphabetically tries
2796	The words _bear, bridge, fir, darkness, bog,
2797	Raven, snowstorm, tempest, fog,
2798	Et cetera_; but nothing showed
2799	Her Martin Zadeka in aid,
2800	Though the foul vision promise made
2801	Of a most mournful episode,
2802	And many a day thereafter laid
2803	A load of care upon the maid."But lo! forth from the valleys dun
2804	With purple hand Aurora leads,
2805	Swift following in her wake, the sun,"
2806	And a grand festival proceeds.
2807	The Larinas were since sunrise
2808	O'erwhelmed with guests; by families
2809	The neighbours come, in sledge approach,
2810	Britzka, kibitka, or in coach.
2811	Crush and confusion in the hall,
2812	Latest arrivals' salutations,
2813	Barking, young ladies' osculations,
2814	Shouts, laughter, jamming 'gainst the wall,
2815	Bows and the scrape of many feet,
2816	Nurses who scream and babes who bleat.
2817	Bringing his partner corpulent
2818	Fat Poustiakoff drove to the door;
2819	Gvozdine, a landlord excellent,
2820	Oppressor of the wretched poor;
2821	And the Skatenines, aged pair,
2822	With all their progeny were there,
2823	Who from two years to thirty tell;
2824	Petoushkoff, the provincial swell;
2825	Bouyanoff too, my cousin, wore
2826	His wadded coat and cap with peak;
2827	And Flianoff, pensioned councillor,
2828	Rogue and extortioner of yore,
2829	Now buffoon, glutton, and a bore.
2830	The family of Kharlikoff,
2831	Came with Monsieur Triquet, a prig,
2832	Who arrived lately from Tamboff,
2833	In spectacles and chestnut wig.
2834	Like a true Frenchman, couplets wrought
2835	In Tania's praise in pouch he brought,
2836	Known unto children perfectly:
2837	_Reveillez-vouz, belle endormie_.
2838	Among some ancient ballads thrust,
2839	He found them in an almanac,
2840	And the sagacious Triquet back
2841	To light had brought them from their dust,
2842	Whilst he "belle Nina" had the face
2843	By "belle Tattiana" to replace.Lo! from the nearest barrack came,
2844	Of old maids the divinity,
2845	And comfort of each country dame,
2846	The captain of a company.
2847	He enters. Ah! good news to-day!
2848	The military band will play.
2849	The colonel sent it. Oh! delight!
2850	So there will be a dance to-night.
2851	Girls in anticipation skip!
2852	But dinner-time comes. Two and two
2853	They hand in hand to table go.
2854	The maids beside Tattiana keep--
2855	Men opposite. The cross they sign
2856	And chattering loud sit down to dine.Ceased for a space all chattering.
2857	Jaws are at work. On every side
2858	Plates, knives and forks are clattering
2859	And ringing wine-glasses are plied.
2860	But by degrees the crowd begin
2861	To raise a clamour and a din:
2862	They laugh, they argue, and they bawl,
2863	They shout and no one lists at all.
2864	The doors swing open: Lenski makes
2865	His entrance with Oneguine. "Ah!
2866	At last the author!" cries Mamma.
2867	The guests make room; aside each takes
2868	His chair, plate, knife and fork in haste;
2869	The friends are called and quickly placed.Right opposite Tattiana placed,
2870	She, than the morning moon more pale,
2871	More timid than a doe long chased,
2872	Lifts not her eyes which swimming fail.
2873	Anew the flames of passion start
2874	Within her; she is sick at heart;
2875	The two friends' compliments she hears
2876	Not, and a flood of bitter tears
2877	With effort she restrains. Well nigh
2878	The poor girl fell into a faint,
2879	But strength of mind and self-restraint
2880	Prevailed at last. She in reply
2881	Said something in an undertone
2882	And at the table sat her down.To tragedy, the fainting fit,
2883	And female tears hysterical,
2884	Oneguine could not now submit,
2885	For long he had endured them all.
2886	Our misanthrope was full of ire,
2887	At a great feast against desire,
2888	And marking Tania's agitation,
2889	Cast down his eyes in trepidation
2890	And sulked in silent indignation;
2891	Swearing how Lenski he would rile,
2892	Avenge himself in proper style.
2893	Triumphant by anticipation,
2894	Caricatures he now designed
2895	Of all the guests within his mind.Certainly not Eugene alone
2896	Tattiana's trouble might have spied,
2897	But that the eyes of every one
2898	By a rich pie were occupied--
2899	Unhappily too salt by far;
2900	And that a bottle sealed with tar
2901	Appeared, Don's effervescing boast,
2902	Between the blanc-mange and the roast;
2903	Behind, of glasses an array,
2904	Tall, slender, like thy form designed,
2905	Zizi, thou mirror of my mind,
2906	Fair object of my guileless lay,
2907	Seductive cup of love, whose flow
2908	Made me so tipsy long ago!
2909	From the moist cork the bottle freed
2910	With loud explosion, the bright wine
2911	Hissed forth. With serious air indeed,
2912	Long tortured by his lay divine,
2913	Triquet arose, and for the bard
2914	The company deep silence guard.
2915	Tania well nigh expired when he
2916	Turned to her and discordantly
2917	Intoned it, manuscript in hand.
2918	Voices and hands applaud, and she
2919	Must bow in common courtesy;
2920	The poet, modest though so grand,
2921	Drank to her health in the first place,
2922	Then handed her the song with grace.Congratulations, toasts resound,
2923	Tattiana thanks to all returned,
2924	But, when Oneguine's turn came round,
2925	The maiden's weary eye which yearned,
2926	Her agitation and distress
2927	Aroused in him some tenderness.
2928	He bowed to her nor silence broke,
2929	But somehow there shone in his look
2930	The witching light of sympathy;
2931	I know not if his heart felt pain
2932	Or if he meant to flirt again,
2933	From habit or maliciously,
2934	But kindness from his eye had beamed
2935	And to revive Tattiana seemed.The chairs are thrust back with a roar,
2936	The crowd unto the drawing-room speeds,
2937	As bees who leave their dainty store
2938	And seek in buzzing swarms the meads.
2939	Contented and with victuals stored,
2940	Neighbour by neighbour sat and snored,
2941	Matrons unto the fireplace go,
2942	Maids in the corner whisper low;
2943	Behold! green tables are brought forth,
2944	And testy gamesters do engage
2945	In boston and the game of age,
2946	Ombre, and whist all others worth:
2947	A strong resemblance these possess--
2948	All sons of mental weariness.Eight rubbers were already played,
2949	Eight times the heroes of the fight
2950	Change of position had essayed,
2951	When tea was brought. 'Tis my delight
2952	Time to denote by dinner, tea,
2953	And supper. In the country we
2954	Can count the time without much fuss--
2955	The stomach doth admonish us.
2956	And, by the way, I here assert
2957	That for that matter in my verse
2958	As many dinners I rehearse,
2959	As oft to meat and drink advert,
2960	As thou, great Homer, didst of yore,
2961	Whom thirty centuries adore.I will with thy divinity
2962	Contend with knife and fork and platter,
2963	But grant with magnanimity
2964	I'm beaten in another matter;
2965	Thy heroes, sanguinary wights,
2966	Also thy rough-and-tumble fights,
2967	Thy Venus and thy Jupiter,
2968	More advantageously appear
2969	Than cold Oneguine's oddities,
2970	The aspect of a landscape drear.
2971	Or e'en Istomina, my dear,
2972	And fashion's gay frivolities;
2973	But my Tattiana, on my soul,
2974	Is sweeter than thy Helen foul.No one the contrary will urge,
2975	Though for his Helen Menelaus
2976	Again a century should scourge
2977	Us, and like Trojan warriors slay us;
2978	Though around honoured Priam's throne
2979	Troy's sages should in concert own
2980	Once more, when she appeared in sight,
2981	Paris and Menelaus right.
2982	But as to fighting--'twill appear!
2983	For patience, reader, I must plead!
2984	A little farther please to read
2985	And be not in advance severe.
2986	There'll be a fight. I do not lie.
2987	My word of honour given have I.The tea, as I remarked, appeared,
2988	But scarce had maids their saucers ta'en
2989	When in the grand saloon was heard
2990	Of bassoons and of flutes the strain.
2991	His soul by crash of music fired,
2992	His tea with rum no more desired,
2993	The Paris of those country parts
2994	To Olga Petoushkova darts:
2995	To Tania Lenski; Kharlikova,
2996	A marriageable maid matured,
2997	The poet from Tamboff secured,
2998	Bouyanoff whisked off Poustiakova.
2999	All to the grand saloon are gone--
3000	The ball in all its splendour shone.I tried when I began this tale,,
3001	A ball in Peter's capital,
3002	To sketch ye in Albano's style.
3003	But by fantastic dreams distraught,
3004	My memory wandered wide and sought
3005	The feet of my dear lady friends.
3006	O feet, where'er your path extends
3007	I long enough deceived have erred.
3008	The perfidies I recollect
3009	Should make me much more circumspect,
3010	Reform me both in deed and word,
3011	And this fifth canto ought to be
3012	From such digressions wholly free.
3013	The whirlwind of the waltz sweeps by,
3014	Undeviating and insane
3015	As giddy youth's hilarity--
3016	Pair after pair the race sustain.
3017	The moment for revenge, meanwhile,
3018	Espying, Eugene with a smile
3019	Approaches Olga and the pair
3020	Amid the company career.
3021	Soon the maid on a chair he seats,
3022	Begins to talk of this and that,
3023	But when two minutes she had sat,
3024	Again the giddy waltz repeats.
3025	All are amazed; but Lenski he
3026	Scarce credits what his eyes can see.Hark! the mazurka. In times past,
3027	When the mazurka used to peal,
3028	All rattled in the ball-room vast,
3029	The parquet cracked beneath the heel,
3030	And jolting jarred the window-frames.
3031	'Tis not so now. Like gentle dames
3032	We glide along a floor of wax.
3033	However, the mazurka lacks
3034	Nought of its charms original
3035	In country towns, where still it keeps
3036	Its stamping, capers and high leaps.
3037	Fashion is there immutable,
3038	Who tyrannizes us with ease,
3039	Of modern Russians the disease.Bouyanoff, wrathful cousin mine,
3040	Unto the hero of this lay
3041	Olga and Tania led. Malign,
3042	Oneguine Olga bore away.
3043	Gliding in negligent career,
3044	He bending whispered in her ear
3045	Some madrigal not worth a rush,
3046	And pressed her hand--the crimson blush
3047	Upon her cheek by adulation
3048	Grew brighter still. But Lenski hath
3049	Seen all, beside himself with wrath,
3050	And hot with jealous indignation,
3051	Till the mazurka's close he stays,
3052	Her hand for the cotillon prays.
3053	She fears she cannot.--Cannot? Why?--
3054	She promised Eugene, or she would
3055	With great delight.--O God on high!
3056	Heard he the truth? And thus she could--
3057	And can it be? But late a child
3058	And now a fickle flirt and wild,
3059	Cunning already to display
3060	And well-instructed to betray!
3061	Lenski the stroke could not sustain,
3062	At womankind he growled a curse,
3063	Departed, ordered out his horse
3064	And galloped home. But pistols twain,
3065	A pair of bullets--nought beside--
3066	His fate shall presently decide.
3067	Having remarked Vladimir's flight,
3068	Oneguine, bored to death again,
3069	By Olga stood, dejected quite
3070	And satisfied with vengeance ta'en.
3071	Olga began to long likewise
3072	For Lenski, sought him with her eyes,
3073	And endless the cotillon seemed
3074	As if some troubled dream she dreamed.
3075	'Tis done. To supper they proceed.
3076	Bedding is laid out and to all
3077	Assigned a lodging, from the hall
3078	Up to the attic, and all need
3079	Tranquil repose. Eugene alone
3080	To pass the night at home hath gone.
3081	All slumber. In the drawing-room
3082	Loud snores the cumbrous Poustiakoff
3083	With better half as cumbersome;
3084	Gvozdine, Bouyanoff, Petoushkoff
3085	And Flianoff, somewhat indisposed,
3086	On chairs in the saloon reposed,
3087	Whilst on the floor Monsieur Triquet
3088	In jersey and in nightcap lay.
3089	In Olga's and Tattiana's rooms
3090	Lay all the girls by sleep embraced,
3091	Except one by the window placed
3092	Whom pale Diana's ray illumes--
3093	My poor Tattiana cannot sleep
3094	But stares into the darkness deep.
3095	His visit she had not awaited,
3096	His momentary loving glance
3097	Her inmost soul had penetrated,
3098	And his strange conduct at the dance
3099	With Olga; nor of this appeared
3100	An explanation: she was scared,
3101	Alarmed by jealous agonies:
3102	A hand of ice appeared to seize
3103	Her heart: it seemed a darksome pit
3104	Beneath her roaring opened wide:
3105	"I shall expire," Tattiana cried,
3106	"But death from him will be delight.
3107	I murmur not! Why mournfulness?
3108	He _cannot_ give me happiness."
3109	Haste, haste thy lagging pace, my story!
3110	A new acquaintance we must scan.
3111	There dwells five versts from Krasnogory,
3112	Vladimir's property, a man
3113	Who thrives this moment as I write,
3114	A philosophic anchorite:
3115	Zaretski, once a bully bold,
3116	A gambling troop when he controlled,
3117	Chief rascal, pot-house president,
3118	Now of a family the head,
3119	Simple and kindly and unwed,
3120	True friend, landlord benevolent,
3121	Yea! and a man of honour, lo!
3122	How perfect doth our epoch grow!
3123	Time was the flattering voice of fame,
3124	His ruffian bravery adored,
3125	And true, his pistol's faultless aim
3126	An ace at fifteen paces bored.
3127	But I must add to what I write
3128	That, tipsy once in actual fight,
3129	He from his Kalmuck horse did leap
3130	In mud and mire to wallow deep,
3131	Drunk as a fly; and thus the French
3132	A valuable hostage gained,
3133	A modern Regulus unchained,
3134	Who to surrender did not blench
3135	That every morn at Verrey's cost
3136	Three flasks of wine he might exhaust.
3137	Time was, his raillery was gay,
3138	He loved the simpleton to mock,
3139	To make wise men the idiot play
3140	Openly or 'neath decent cloak.
3141	Yet sometimes this or that deceit
3142	Encountered punishment complete,
3143	And sometimes into snares as well
3144	Himself just like a greenhorn fell.
3145	He could in disputation shine
3146	With pungent or obtuse retort,
3147	At times to silence would resort,
3148	At times talk nonsense with design;
3149	Quarrels among young friends he bred
3150	And to the field of honour led;
3151	Or reconciled them, it may be,
3152	And all the three to breakfast went;
3153	Then he'd malign them secretly
3154	With jest and gossip gaily blent.
3155	_Sed alia tempora_. And bravery
3156	Diminishes as years decline.
3157	But, as I said, Zaretski mine
3158	Beneath acacias, cherry-trees,
3159	From storms protection having sought,
3160	Lived as a really wise man ought,
3161	Like Horace, planted cabbages,
3162	Both ducks and geese in plenty bred
3163	And lessons to his children read.
3164	He was no fool, and Eugene mine,
3165	To friendship making no pretence,
3166	Admired his judgment, which was fine,
3167	Pervaded with much common sense.
3168	He usually was glad to see
3169	The man and liked his company,
3170	So, when he came next day to call,
3171	Was not surprised thereby at all.
3172	But, after mutual compliments,
3173	Zaretski with a knowing grin,
3174	Ere conversation could begin,
3175	The epistle from the bard presents.
3176	Oneguine to the window went
3177	And scanned in silence its content.
3178	It was a cheery, generous
3179	Cartel, or challenge to a fight,
3180	Whereto in language courteous
3181	Lenski his comrade did invite.
3182	Oneguine, by first impulse moved,
3183	Turned and replied as it behoved,
3184	Curtly announcing for the fray
3185	That he was "ready any day."
3186	Zaretski rose, nor would explain,
3187	He cared no longer there to stay,
3188	Had much to do at home that day,
3189	And so departed. But Eugene,
3190	The matter by his conscience tried,
3191	Was with himself dissatisfied.In fact, the subject analysed,
3192	Within that secret court discussed,
3193	In much his conduct stigmatized;
3194	For, from the outset, 'twas unjust
3195	To jest as he had done last eve,
3196	A timid, shrinking love to grieve.
3197	And ought he not to disregard
3198	The poet's madness? for 'tis hard
3199	At eighteen not to play the fool!
3200	Sincerely loving him, Eugene
3201	Assuredly should not have been
3202	Conventionality's dull tool--
3203	Not a mere hot, pugnacious boy,
3204	But man of sense and probity.He might his motives have narrated,
3205	Not bristled up like a wild beast,
3206	He ought to have conciliated
3207	That youthful heart--"But, now at least,
3208	The opportunity is flown.
3209	Besides, a duellist well-known
3210	Hath mixed himself in the affair,
3211	Malicious and a slanderer.
3212	Undoubtedly, disdain alone
3213	Should recompense his idle jeers,
3214	But fools--their calumnies and sneers"--
3215	Behold! the world's opinion!
3216	Our idol, Honour's motive force,
3217	Round which revolves the universe.
3218	Impatient, boiling o'er with wrath,
3219	The bard his answer waits at home,
3220	But lo! his braggart neighbour hath
3221	Triumphant with the answer come.
3222	Now for the jealous youth what joy!
3223	He feared the criminal might try
3224	To treat the matter as a jest,
3225	Use subterfuge, and thus his breast
3226	From the dread pistol turn away.
3227	But now all doubt was set aside,
3228	Unto the windmill he must ride
3229	To-morrow before break of day,
3230	To cock the pistol; barrel bend
3231	On thigh or temple, friend on friend.Resolved the flirt to cast away,
3232	The foaming Lenski would refuse,
3233	To see his Olga ere the fray--
3234	His watch, the sun in turn he views--
3235	Finally tost his arms in air
3236	And lo! he is already there!
3237	He deemed his coming would inspire
3238	Olga with trepidation dire.
3239	He was deceived. Just as before
3240	The miserable bard to meet,
3241	As hope uncertain and as sweet,
3242	Olga ran skipping from the door.
3243	She was as heedless and as gay--
3244	Well! just as she was yesterday."Why did you leave last night so soon?"
3245	Was the first question Olga made,
3246	Lenski, into confusion thrown,
3247	All silently hung down his head.
3248	Jealousy and vexation took
3249	To flight before her radiant look,
3250	Before such fond simplicity
3251	And mental elasticity.
3252	He eyed her with a fond concern,
3253	Perceived that he was still beloved,
3254	Already by repentance moved
3255	To ask forgiveness seemed to yearn;
3256	But trembles, words he cannot find,
3257	Delighted, almost sane in mind.But once more pensive and distressed
3258	Beside his Olga doth he grieve,
3259	Nor enough strength of mind possessed
3260	To mention the foregoing eve,
3261	He mused: "I will her saviour be!
3262	With ardent sighs and flattery
3263	The vile seducer shall not dare
3264	The freshness of her heart impair,
3265	Nor shall the caterpillar come
3266	The lily's stem to eat away,
3267	Nor shall the bud of yesterday
3268	Perish when half disclosed its bloom!"--
3269	All this, my friends, translate aright:
3270	"I with my friend intend to fight!"If he had only known the wound
3271	Which rankled in Tattiana's breast,
3272	And if Tattiana mine had found--
3273	If the poor maiden could have guessed
3274	That the two friends with morning's light
3275	Above the yawning grave would fight,--
3276	Ah! it may be, affection true
3277	Had reconciled the pair anew!
3278	But of this love, e'en casually,
3279	As yet none had discovered aught;
3280	Eugene of course related nought,
3281	Tattiana suffered secretly;
3282	Her nurse, who could have made a guess,
3283	Was famous for thick-headedness.Lenski that eve in thought immersed,
3284	Now gloomy seemed and cheerful now,
3285	But he who by the Muse was nursed
3286	Is ever thus. With frowning brow
3287	To the pianoforte he moves
3288	And various chords upon it proves,
3289	Then, eyeing Olga, whispers low:
3290	"I'm happy, say, is it not so?"--
3291	But it grew late; he must not stay;
3292	Heavy his heart with anguish grew;
3293	To the young girl he said adieu,
3294	As it were, tore himself away.
3295	Gazing into his face, she said:
3296	"What ails thee?"--"Nothing."--He is fled.At home arriving he addressed
3297	His care unto his pistols' plight,
3298	Replaced them in their box, undressed
3299	And Schiller read by candlelight.
3300	But one thought only filled his mind,
3301	His mournful heart no peace could find,
3302	Olga he sees before his eyes
3303	Miraculously fair arise,
3304	Vladimir closes up his book,
3305	And grasps a pen: his verse, albeit
3306	With lovers' rubbish filled, was neat
3307	And flowed harmoniously. He took
3308	And spouted it with lyric fire--
3309	Like D when dinner doth inspire.Destiny hath preserved his lay.
3310	I have it. Lo! the very thing!
3311	"Oh! whither have ye winged your way,
3312	Ye golden days of my young spring?
3313	What will the coming dawn reveal?
3314	In vain my anxious eyes appeal;
3315	In mist profound all yet is hid.
3316	So be it! Just the laws which bid
3317	The fatal bullet penetrate,
3318	Or innocently past me fly.
3319	Good governs all! The hour draws nigh
3320	Of life or death predestinate.
3321	Blest be the labours of the light,
3322	And blest the shadows of the night."To-morrow's dawn will glimmer gray,
3323	Bright day will then begin to burn,
3324	But the dark sepulchre I may
3325	Have entered never to return.
3326	The memory of the bard, a dream,
3327	Will be absorbed by Lethe's stream;
3328	Men will forget me, but my urn
3329	To visit, lovely maid, return,
3330	O'er my remains to drop a tear,
3331	And think: here lies who loved me well,
3332	For consecrate to me he fell
3333	In the dawn of existence drear.
3334	Maid whom my heart desires alone,
3335	Approach, approach; I am thine own."Thus in a style _obscure_ and _stale_,
3336	He wrote ('tis the romantic style,
3337	Though of romance therein I fail
3338	To see aught--never mind meanwhile)
3339	And about dawn upon his breast
3340	His weary head declined at rest,
3341	For o'er a word to fashion known,
3342	"Ideal," he had drowsy grown.
3343	But scarce had sleep's soft witchery
3344	Subdued him, when his neighbour stept
3345	Into the chamber where he slept
3346	And wakened him with the loud cry:
3347	"'Tis time to get up! Seven doth strike.
3348	Oneguine waits on us, 'tis like."
3349	He was in error; for Eugene
3350	Was sleeping then a sleep like death;
3351	The pall of night was growing thin,
3352	To Lucifer the cock must breathe
3353	His song, when still he slumbered deep,
3354	The sun had mounted high his steep,
3355	A passing snowstorm wreathed away
3356	With pallid light, but Eugene lay
3357	Upon his couch insensibly;
3358	Slumber still o'er him lingering flies.
3359	But finally he oped his eyes
3360	And turned aside the drapery;
3361	He gazed upon the clock which showed
3362	He long should have been on the road.He rings in haste; in haste arrives
3363	His Frenchman, good Monsieur Guillot,
3364	Who dressing-gown and slippers gives
3365	And linen on him doth bestow.
3366	Dressing as quickly as he can,
3367	Eugene directs the trusty man
3368	To accompany him and to escort
3369	A box of terrible import.
3370	Harnessed the rapid sledge arrived:
3371	He enters: to the mill he drives:
3372	Descends, the order Guillot gives,
3373	The fatal tubes Lepage contrived
3374	To bring behind: the triple steeds
3375	To two young oaks the coachman leads.
3376	Lenski the foeman's apparition
3377	Leaning against the dam expects,
3378	Zaretski, village mechanician,
3379	In the meantime the mill inspects.
3380	Oneguine his excuses says;
3381	"But," cried Zaretski in amaze,
3382	"Your second you have left behind!"
3383	A duellist of classic mind,
3384	Method was dear unto his heart
3385	He would not that a man ye slay
3386	In a lax or informal way,
3387	But followed the strict rules of art,
3388	And ancient usages observed
3389	."My second!" cried in turn Eugene,
3390	"Behold my friend Monsieur Guillot;
3391	To this arrangement can be seen,
3392	No obstacle of which I know.
3393	Although unknown to fame mayhap,
3394	He's a straightforward little chap."
3395	Zaretski bit his lip in wrath,
3396	But to Vladimir Eugene saith:
3397	"Shall we commence?"--"Let it be so,"
3398	Lenski replied, and soon they be
3399	Behind the mill. Meantime ye see
3400	Zaretski and Monsieur Guillot
3401	In consultation stand aside--
3402	The foes with downcast eyes abide.Foes! Is it long since friendship rent
3403	Asunder was and hate prepared?
3404	Since leisure was together spent,
3405	Meals, secrets, occupations shared?
3406	Now, like hereditary foes,
3407	Malignant fury they disclose,
3408	As in some frenzied dream of fear
3409	These friends cold-bloodedly draw near
3410	Mutual destruction to contrive.
3411	Cannot they amicably smile
3412	Ere crimson stains their hands defile,
3413	Depart in peace and friendly live?
3414	But fashionable hatred's flame
3415	Trembles at artificial shame.The shining pistols are uncased,
3416	The mallet loud the ramrod strikes,
3417	Bullets are down the barrels pressed,
3418	For the first time the hammer clicks.
3419	Lo! poured in a thin gray cascade,
3420	The powder in the pan is laid,
3421	The sharp flint, screwed securely on,
3422	Is cocked once more. Uneasy grown,
3423	Guillot behind a pollard stood;
3424	Aside the foes their mantles threw,
3425	Zaretski paces thirty-two
3426	Measured with great exactitude.
3427	At each extreme one takes his stand,
3428	A loaded pistol in his hand."Advance!"--
3429	    Indifferent and sedate,
3430	The foes, as yet not taking aim,
3431	With measured step and even gait
3432	Athwart the snow four paces came--
3433	Four deadly paces do they span;
3434	Oneguine slowly then began
3435	To raise his pistol to his eye,
3436	Though he advanced unceasingly.
3437	And lo! five paces more they pass,
3438	And Lenski, closing his left eye,
3439	Took aim--but as immediately
3440	Oneguine fired--Alas! alas!
3441	The poet's hour hath sounded--See!
3442	He drops his pistol silently.He on his bosom gently placed
3443	His hand, and fell. His clouded eye
3444	Not agony, but death expressed.
3445	So from the mountain lazily
3446	The avalanche of snow first bends,
3447	Then glittering in the sun descends.
3448	The cold sweat bursting from his brow,
3449	To the youth Eugene hurried now--
3450	Gazed on him, called him. Useless care!
3451	He was no more! The youthful bard
3452	For evermore had disappeared.
3453	The storm was hushed. The blossom fair
3454	Was withered ere the morning light--
3455	The altar flame was quenched in night.Tranquil he lay, and strange to view
3456	The peace which on his forehead beamed,
3457	His breast was riddled through and through,
3458	The blood gushed from the wound and steamed
3459	Ere this but one brief moment beat
3460	That heart with inspiration sweet
3461	And enmity and hope and love--
3462	The blood boiled and the passions strove.
3463	Now, as in a deserted house,
3464	All dark and silent hath become;
3465	The inmate is for ever dumb,
3466	The windows whitened, shutters close--
3467	Whither departed is the host?
3468	God knows! The very trace is lost.'Tis sweet the foe to aggravate
3469	With epigrams impertinent,
3470	Sweet to behold him obstinate,
3471	His butting horns in anger bent,
3472	The glass unwittingly inspect
3473	And blush to own himself reflect.
3474	Sweeter it is, my friends, if he
3475	Howl like a dolt: 'tis meant for me!
3476	But sweeter still it is to arrange
3477	For him an honourable grave,
3478	At his pale brow a shot to have,
3479	Placed at the customary range;
3480	But home his body to despatch
3481	Can scarce in sweetness be a match.Well, if your pistol ball by chance
3482	The comrade of your youth should strike,
3483	Who by a haughty word or glance
3484	Or any trifle else ye like
3485	You o'er your wine insulted hath--
3486	Or even overcome by wrath
3487	Scornfully challenged you afield--
3488	Tell me, of sentiments concealed
3489	Which in your spirit dominates,
3490	When motionless your gaze beneath
3491	He lies, upon his forehead death,
3492	And slowly life coagulates--
3493	When deaf and silent he doth lie
3494	Heedless of your despairing cry?Eugene, his pistol yet in hand
3495	And with remorseful anguish filled,
3496	Gazing on Lenski's corse did stand--
3497	Zaretski shouted: "Why, he's killed!"--
3498	Killed! at this dreadful exclamation
3499	Oneguine went with trepidation
3500	And the attendants called in haste.
3501	Most carefully Zaretski placed
3502	Within his sledge the stiffened corse,
3503	And hurried home his awful freight.
3504	Conscious of death approximate,
3505	Loud paws the earth each panting horse,
3506	His bit with foam besprinkled o'er,
3507	And homeward like an arrow tore.My friends, the poet ye regret!
3508	When hope's delightful flower but bloomed
3509	In bud of promise incomplete,
3510	The manly toga scarce assumed,
3511	He perished. Where his troubled dreams,
3512	And where the admirable streams
3513	Of youthful impulse, reverie,
3514	Tender and elevated, free?
3515	And where tempestuous love's desires,
3516	The thirst of knowledge and of fame,
3517	Horror of sinfulness and shame,
3518	Imagination's sacred fires,
3519	Ye shadows of a life more high,
3520	Ye dreams of heavenly poesy?Perchance to benefit mankind,
3521	Or but for fame he saw the light;
3522	His lyre, to silence now consigned,
3523	Resounding through all ages might
3524	Have echoed to eternity.
3525	With worldly honours, it may be,
3526	Fortune the poet had repaid.
3527	It may be that his martyred shade
3528	Carried a truth divine away;
3529	That, for the century designed,
3530	Had perished a creative mind,
3531	And past the threshold of decay,
3532	He ne'er shall hear Time's eulogy,
3533	The blessings of humanity.Or, it may be, the bard had passed
3534	A life in common with the rest;
3535	Vanished his youthful years at last,
3536	The fire extinguished in his breast,
3537	In many things had changed his life--
3538	The Muse abandoned, ta'en a wife,
3539	Inhabited the country, clad
3540	In dressing-gown, a cuckold glad:
3541	A life of fact, not fiction, led--
3542	At forty suffered from the gout,
3543	Eaten, drunk, gossiped and grown stout:
3544	And finally, upon his bed
3545	Had finished life amid his sons,
3546	Doctors and women, sobs and groans.But, howsoe'er his lot were cast,
3547	Alas! the youthful lover slain,
3548	Poetical enthusiast,
3549	A friendly hand thy life hath ta'en!
3550	There is a spot the village near
3551	Where dwelt the Muses' worshipper,
3552	Two pines have joined their tangled roots,
3553	A rivulet beneath them shoots
3554	Its waters to the neighbouring vale.
3555	There the tired ploughman loves to lie,
3556	The reaping girls approach and ply
3557	Within its wave the sounding pail,
3558	And by that shady rivulet
3559	A simple tombstone hath been set.There, when the rains of spring we mark
3560	Upon the meadows showering,
3561	The shepherd plaits his shoe of bark,
3562	Of Volga fishermen doth sing,
3563	And the young damsel from the town,
3564	For summer to the country flown,
3565	Whene'er across the plain at speed
3566	Alone she gallops on her steed,
3567	Stops at the tomb in passing by;
3568	The tightened leathern rein she draws,
3569	Aside she casts her veil of gauze
3570	And reads with rapid eager eye
3571	The simple epitaph--a tear
3572	Doth in her gentle eye appear.
3573	And meditative from the spot
3574	She leisurely away doth ride,
3575	Spite of herself with Lenski's lot
3576	Longtime her mind is occupied.
3577	She muses: "What was Olga's fate?
3578	Longtime was her heart desolate
3579	Or did her tears soon cease to flow?
3580	And where may be her sister now?
3581	Where is the outlaw, banned by men,
3582	Of fashionable dames the foe,
3583	The misanthrope of gloomy brow,
3584	By whom the youthful bard was slain?"--
3585	In time I'll give ye without fail
3586	A true account and in detail.But not at present, though sincerely
3587	I on my chosen hero dote;
3588	Though I'll return to him right early,
3589	Just at this moment I cannot.
3590	Years have inclined me to stern prose,
3591	Years to light rhyme themselves oppose,
3592	And now, I mournfully confess,
3593	In rhyming I show laziness.
3594	As once, to fill the rapid page
3595	My pen no longer finds delight,
3596	Other and colder thoughts affright,
3597	Sterner solicitudes engage,
3598	In worldly din or solitude
3599	Upon my visions such intrude.Fresh aspirations I have known,
3600	I am acquainted with fresh care,
3601	Hopeless are all the first, I own,
3602	Yet still remains the old despair.
3603	Illusions, dream, where, where your sweetness?
3604	Where youth ?
3605	And is it true her garland bright
3606	At last is shrunk and withered quite?
3607	And is it true and not a jest,
3608	Not even a poetic phrase,
3609	That vanished are my youthful days,
3610	Never for me to reappear--
3611	That soon I reach my thirtieth year?And so my noon hath come! If so,
3612	I must resign myself, in sooth;
3613	Yet let us part in friendship, O
3614	My frivolous and jolly youth.
3615	I thank thee for thy joyfulness,
3616	Love's tender transports and distress,
3617	For riot, frolics, mighty feeds,
3618	And all that from thy hand proceeds--
3619	I thank thee. In thy company,
3620	With tumult or contentment still
3621	Of thy delights I drank my fill,
3622	Enough! with tranquil spirit I
3623	Commence a new career in life
3624	And rest from bygone days of strife.But pause! Thou calm retreats, farewell,
3625	Where my days in the wilderness
3626	Of languor and of love did tell
3627	And contemplative dreaminess;
3628	And thou, youth's early inspiration,
3629	Invigorate imagination
3630	And spur my spirit's torpid mood!
3631	Fly frequent to my solitude,
3632	Let not the poet's spirit freeze,
3633	Grow harsh and cruel, dead and dry,
3634	Eventually petrify
3635	In the world's mortal revelries,
3636	Amid the soulless sons of pride
3637	And glittering simpletons beside;Amid sly, pusillanimous
3638	Spoiled children most degenerate
3639	And tiresome rogues ridiculous
3640	And stupid censors passionate;
3641	Amid coquettes who pray to God
3642	And abject slaves who kiss the rod;
3643	In haunts of fashion where each day
3644	All with urbanity betray,
3645	Where harsh frivolity proclaims
3646	Its cold unfeeling sentences;
3647	Amid the awful emptiness
3648	Of conversation, thought and aims--
3649	In that morass where you and I
3650	Wallow, my friends, in company!
3651	Moscow
3652	Moscow, Russia's darling daughter,
3653	Where thine equal shall we find?
3654	                    Dmitrieff
3655	Who can help loving mother Moscow?
3656	            Baratynski
3657	A journey to Moscow! To see the world!
3658	Where better?
3659	        Where man is not.
3660	    Griboyedoff
3661	Impelled by Spring's dissolving beams,
3662	The snows from off the hills around
3663	Descended swift in turbid streams
3664	And flooded all the level ground.
3665	A smile from slumbering nature clear
3666	Did seem to greet the youthful year;
3667	The heavens shone in deeper blue,
3668	The woods, still naked to the view,
3669	Seemed in a haze of green embowered.
3670	The bee forth from his cell of wax
3671	Flew to collect his rural tax;
3672	The valleys dried and gaily flowered;
3673	Herds low, and under night's dark veil
3674	Already sings the nightingale.
3675	Mournful is thine approach to me,
3676	O Spring, thou chosen time of love!
3677	What agitation languidly
3678	My spirit and my blood doth move,
3679	What sad emotions o'er me steal
3680	When first upon my cheek I feel
3681	The breath of Spring again renewed,
3682	Secure in rural quietude--
3683	Or, strange to me is happiness?
3684	Do all things which to mirth incline.
3685	And make a dark existence shine
3686	Inflict annoyance and distress
3687	Upon a soul inert and cloyed?--
3688	And is all light within destroyed?
3689	Or, heedless of the leaves' return
3690	Which Autumn late to earth consigned,
3691	Do we alone our losses mourn
3692	Of which the rustling woods remind?
3693	Or, when anew all Nature teems,
3694	Do we foresee in troubled dreams
3695	The coming of life's Autumn drear.
3696	For which no springtime shall appear?
3697	Or, it may be, we inly seek,
3698	Wafted upon poetic wing,
3699	Some other long-departed Spring,
3700	Whose memories make the heart beat quick
3701	With thoughts of a far distant land,
3702	Of a strange night when the moon and--
3703	'Tis now the season! Idlers all,
3704	Epicurean philosophers,
3705	Ye men of fashion cynical,
3706	Of Levshin's school ye followers,
3707	Priams of country populations
3708	And dames of fine organisations,
3709	Spring summons you to her green bowers,
3710	'Tis the warm time of labour, flowers;
3711	The time for mystic strolls which late
3712	Into the starry night extend.
3713	Quick to the country let us wend
3714	In vehicles surcharged with freight;
3715	In coach or post-cart duly placed
3716	Beyond the city-barriers haste.Thou also, reader generous,
3717	The chaise long ordered please employ,
3718	Abandon cities riotous,
3719	Which in the winter were a joy:
3720	The Muse capricious let us coax,
3721	Go hear the rustling of the oaks
3722	Beside a nameless rivulet,
3723	Where in the country Eugene yet,
3724	An idle anchorite and sad,
3725	A while ago the winter spent,
3726	Near young Tattiana resident,
3727	My pretty self-deceiving maid--
3728	No more the village knows his face,
3729	For there he left a mournful trace.
3730	Let us proceed unto a rill,
3731	Which in a hilly neighbourhood
3732	Seeks, winding amid meadows still,
3733	The river through the linden wood.
3734	The nightingale there all night long,
3735	Spring's paramour, pours forth her song
3736	The fountain brawls, sweetbriers bloom,
3737	And lo! where lies a marble tomb
3738	And two old pines their branches spread--
3739	"_Vladimir Lenski lies beneath,
3740	Who early died a gallant death_,"
3741	Thereon the passing traveller read:
3742	"_The date, his fleeting years how long--
3743	Repose in peace, thou child of song_."
3744	Time was, the breath of early dawn
3745	Would agitate a mystic wreath
3746	Hung on a pine branch earthward drawn
3747	Above the humble urn of death.
3748	Time was, two maidens from their home
3749	At eventide would hither come,
3750	And, by the light the moonbeams gave,
3751	Lament, embrace upon that grave.
3752	But now--none heeds the monument
3753	Of woe: effaced the pathway now:
3754	There is no wreath upon the bough:
3755	Alone beside it, gray and bent,
3756	As formerly the shepherd sits
3757	And his poor basten sandal knits.
3758	My poor Vladimir, bitter tears
3759	Thee but a little space bewept,
3760	Faithless, alas! thy maid appears,
3761	Nor true unto her sorrow kept.
3762	Another could her heart engage,
3763	Another could her woe assuage
3764	By flattery and lover's art--
3765	A lancer captivates her heart!
3766	A lancer her soul dotes upon:
3767	Before the altar, lo! the pair,
3768	Mark ye with what a modest air
3769	She bows her head beneath the crown;
3770	Behold her downcast eyes which glow,
3771	Her lips where light smiles come and go!
3772	My poor Vladimir! In the tomb,
3773	Passed into dull eternity,
3774	Was the sad poet filled with gloom,
3775	Hearing the fatal perfidy?
3776	Or, beyond Lethe lulled to rest,
3777	Hath the bard, by indifference blest,
3778	Callous to all on earth become--
3779	Is the world to him sealed and dumb?
3780	The same unmoved oblivion
3781	On us beyond the grave attends,
3782	The voice of lovers, foes and friends,
3783	Dies suddenly: of heirs alone
3784	Remains on earth the unseemly rage,
3785	Whilst struggling for the heritage.Soon Olga's accents shrill resound
3786	No longer through her former home;
3787	The lancer, to his calling bound,
3788	Back to his regiment must roam.
3789	The aged mother, bathed in tears,
3790	Distracted by her grief appears
3791	When the hour came to bid good-bye--
3792	But my Tattiana's eyes were dry.
3793	Only her countenance assumed
3794	A deadly pallor, air distressed;
3795	When all around the entrance pressed,
3796	To say farewell, and fussed and fumed
3797	Around the carriage of the pair--
3798	Tattiana gently led them there.And long her eyes as through a haze
3799	After the wedded couple strain;
3800	Alas! the friend of childish days
3801	Away, Tattiana, hath been ta'en.
3802	Thy dove, thy darling little pet
3803	On whom a sister's heart was set
3804	Afar is borne by cruel fate,
3805	For evermore is separate.
3806	She wanders aimless as a sprite,
3807	Into the tangled garden goes
3808	But nowhere can she find repose,
3809	Nor even tears afford respite,
3810	Of consolation all bereft--
3811	Well nigh her heart in twain was cleft.In cruel solitude each day
3812	With flame more ardent passion burns,
3813	And to Oneguine far away
3814	Her heart importunately turns.
3815	She never more his face may view,
3816	For was it not her duty to
3817	Detest him for a brother slain?
3818	The poet fell; already men
3819	No more remembered him; unto
3820	Another his betrothed was given;
3821	The memory of the bard was driven
3822	Like smoke athwart the heaven blue;
3823	Two hearts perchance were desolate
3824	And mourned him still. Why mourn his fate?'Twas eve. 'Twas dusk. The river speeds
3825	In tranquil flow. The beetle hums.
3826	Already dance to song proceeds;
3827	The fisher's fire afar illumes
3828	The river's bank. Tattiana lone
3829	Beneath the silver of the moon
3830	Long time in meditation deep
3831	Her path across the plain doth keep--
3832	Proceeds, until she from a hill
3833	Sees where a noble mansion stood,
3834	A village and beneath, a wood,
3835	A garden by a shining rill.
3836	She gazed thereon, and instant beat
3837	Her heart more loudly and more fleet.She hesitates, in doubt is thrown--
3838	"Shall I proceed, or homeward flee?
3839	He is not there: I am not known:
3840	The house and garden I would see."
3841	Tattiana from the hill descends
3842	With bated breath, around she bends
3843	A countenance perplexed and scared.
3844	She enters a deserted yard--
3845	Yelping, a pack of dogs rush out,
3846	But at her shriek ran forth with noise
3847	The household troop of little boys,
3848	Who with a scuffle and a shout
3849	The curs away to kennel chase,
3850	The damsel under escort place."Can I inspect the mansion, please?"
3851	Tattiana asks, and hurriedly
3852	Unto Anicia for the keys
3853	The family of children hie.
3854	Anicia soon appears, the door
3855	Opens unto her visitor.
3856	Into the lonely house she went,
3857	Wherein a space Oneguine spent.
3858	She gazed--a cue, forgotten long,
3859	Doth on the billiard table rest,
3860	Upon the tumbled sofa placed,
3861	A riding whip. She strolls along.
3862	The beldam saith: "The hearth, by it
3863	The master always used to sit."Departed Lenski here to dine
3864	In winter time would often come.
3865	Please follow this way, lady mine,
3866	This is my master's sitting-room.
3867	'Tis here he slept, his coffee took,
3868	Into accounts would sometimes look,
3869	A book at early morn perused.
3870	The room my former master used.
3871	On Sundays by yon window he,
3872	Spectacles upon nose, all day
3873	Was wont with me at cards to play.
3874	God save his soul eternally
3875	And grant his weary bones their rest
3876	Deep in our mother Earth's chill breast!"Tattiana's eyes with tender gleam
3877	On everything around her gaze,
3878	Of priceless value all things seem
3879	And in her languid bosom raise
3880	A pleasure though with sorrow knit:
3881	The table with its lamp unlit,
3882	The pile of books, with carpet spread
3883	Beneath the window-sill his bed,
3884	The landscape which the moonbeams fret,
3885	The twilight pale which softens all,
3886	Lord Byron's portrait on the wall
3887	And the cast-iron statuette
3888	With folded arms and eyes bent low,
3889	Cocked hat and melancholy brow.
3890	Long in this fashionable cell
3891	Tattiana as enchanted stood;
3892	But it grew late; cold blew the gale;
3893	Dark was the valley and the wood
3894	Slept o'er the river misty grown.
3895	Behind the mountain sank the moon.
3896	Long, long the hour had past when home
3897	Our youthful wanderer should roam.
3898	She hid the trouble of her breast,
3899	Heaved an involuntary sigh
3900	And turned to leave immediately,
3901	But first permission did request
3902	Thither in future to proceed
3903	That certain volumes she might read.Adieu she to the matron said
3904	At the front gates, but in brief space
3905	At early morn returns the maid
3906	To the abandoned dwelling-place.
3907	When in the study's calm retreat,
3908	Wrapt in oblivion complete,
3909	She found herself alone at last,
3910	Longtime her tears flowed thick and fast;
3911	But presently she tried to read;
3912	At first for books was disinclined,
3913	But soon their choice seemed to her mind
3914	Remarkable. She then indeed
3915	Devoured them with an eager zest.
3916	A new world was made manifest!Although we know that Eugene had
3917	Long ceased to be a reading man,
3918	Still certain authors, I may add,
3919	He had excepted from the ban:
3920	The bard of Juan and the Giaour,
3921	With it may be a couple more;
3922	Romances three, in which ye scan
3923	Portrayed contemporary man
3924	As the reflection of his age,
3925	His immorality of mind
3926	To arid selfishness resigned,
3927	A visionary personage
3928	With his exasperated sense,
3929	His energy and impotence.And numerous pages had preserved
3930	The sharp incisions of his nail,
3931	And these the attentive maid observed
3932	With eye precise and without fail.
3933	Tattiana saw with trepidation
3934	By what idea or observation
3935	Oneguine was the most impressed,
3936	In what he merely acquiesced.
3937	Upon those margins she perceived
3938	Oneguine's pencillings. His mind
3939	Made revelations undesigned,
3940	Of what he thought and what believed,
3941	A dagger, asterisk, or note
3942	Interrogation to denote.And my Tattiana now began
3943	To understand by slow degrees
3944	More clearly, God be praised, the man,
3945	Whom autocratic fate's decrees
3946	Had bid her sigh for without hope--
3947	A dangerous, gloomy misanthrope,
3948	Being from hell or heaven sent,
3949	Angel or fiend malevolent.
3950	Which is he? or an imitation,
3951	A bogy conjured up in joke,
3952	A Russian in Childe Harold's cloak,
3953	Of foreign whims the impersonation--
3954	Handbook of fashionable phrase
3955	Or parody of modern ways?Hath she found out the riddle yet?
3956	Hath she a fitting phrase selected?
3957	But time flies and she doth forget
3958	They long at home have her expected--
3959	Whither two neighbouring dames have walked
3960	And a long time about her talked.
3961	"What can be done? She is no child!"
3962	Cried the old dame with anguish filled:
3963	"Olinka is her junior, see.
3964	'Tis time to marry her, 'tis true,
3965	But tell me what am I to do?
3966	To all she answers cruelly--
3967	I will not wed, and ever weeps
3968	And lonely through the forest creeps.""Is she in love?" quoth one. "With whom?
3969	Bouyanoff courted. She refused.
3970	Petoushkoff met the selfsame doom.
3971	The hussar Pykhtin was accused.
3972	How the young imp on Tania doted!
3973	To captivate her how devoted!

3975	O yes! my hopes soon disappeared."

3977	Should go, the market for a maid,
3978	With many a vacancy, 'tis said."--
3979	"Alas! my friend, no revenue!"

3981	If not, the money I will lend."
3982	The venerable dame opined
3983	The counsel good and full of reason,
3984	Her money counted, and designed
