3986	Tattiana learns the intelligence--
3987	Of her provincial innocence
3988	The unaffected traits she now
3989	Unto a carping world must show--
3990	Her toilette's antiquated style,
3991	Her antiquated mode of speech,
3992	For Moscow fops and Circes each
3993	To mark with a contemptuous smile.
3994	Horror! had she not better stay
3995	Deep in the greenwood far away?Arising with the morning's light,
3996	Unto the fields she makes her way,
3997	And with emotional delight
3998	Surveying them, she thus doth say:
3999	"Ye peaceful valleys all, good-bye!
4000	Ye well-known mountain summits high,
4001	Ye groves whose depths I know so well,
4002	Thou beauteous sky above, farewell!
4003	Delicious nature, thee I fly,
4004	The calm existence which I prize
4005	I yield for splendid vanities,
4006	Thou too farewell, my liberty!
4007	Whither and wherefore do I speed
4008	And what will Destiny concede?"Farther Tattiana's walks extend--
4009	'Tis now the hillock now the rill
4010	Their natural attractions lend
4011	To stay the maid against her will.
4012	She the acquaintances she loves,
4013	Her spacious fields and shady groves,
4014	Another visit hastes to pay.
4015	But Summer swiftly fades away
4016	And golden Autumn draweth nigh,
4017	And pallid nature trembling grieves,
4018	A victim decked with golden leaves;
4019	Dark clouds before the north wind fly;
4020	It blew: it howled: till winter e'en
4021	Came forth in all her magic sheen.The snow descends and buries all,
4022	Hangs heavy on the oaken boughs,
4023	A white and undulating pall
4024	O'er hillock and o'er meadow throws.
4025	The channel of the river stilled
4026	As if with eider-down is filled.
4027	The hoar-frost glitters: all rejoice
4028	In mother Winter's strange caprice.
4029	But Tania's heart is not at ease,
4030	Winter's approach she doth not hail
4031	Nor the frost particles inhale
4032	Nor the first snow of winter seize
4033	Her shoulders, breast and face to lave--
4034	Alarm the winter journey gave.The date was fixed though oft postponed,
4035	But ultimately doth approach.
4036	Examined, mended, newly found
4037	Was the old and forgotten coach;
4038	Kibitkas three, the accustomed train,
4039	The household property contain:
4040	Saucepans and mattresses and chairs,
4041	Portmanteaus and preserves in jars,
4042	Feather-beds, also poultry-coops,
4043	Basins and jugs--well! everything
4044	To happiness contributing.
4045	Behold! beside their dwelling groups
4046	Of serfs the farewell wail have given.
4047	Nags eighteen to the door are driven.
4048	These to the coach of state are bound,
4049	Breakfast the busy cooks prepare,
4050	Baggage is heaped up in a mound,
4051	Old women at the coachmen swear.
4052	A bearded postillion astride
4053	A lean and shaggy nag doth ride,
4054	Unto the gates the servants fly
4055	To bid the gentlefolk good-bye.
4056	These take their seats; the coach of state
4057	Leisurely through the gateway glides.
4058	"Adieu! thou home where peace abides,
4059	Where turmoil cannot penetrate,
4060	Shall I behold thee once again?"--
4061	Tattiana tears cannot restrain.The limits of enlightenment
4062	When to enlarge we shall succeed,
4063	In course of time (the whole extent
4064	Will not five centuries exceed
4065	By computation) it is like
4066	Our roads transformed the eye will strike;
4067	Highways all Russia will unite
4068	And form a network left and right;
4069	On iron bridges we shall gaze
4070	Which o'er the waters boldly leap,
4071	Mountains we'll level and through deep
4072	Streams excavate subaqueous ways,
4073	And Christian folk will, I expect,
4074	An inn at every stage erect.But now, what wretched roads one sees,
4075	Our bridges long neglected rot,
4076	And at the stages bugs and fleas
4077	One moment's slumber suffer not.
4078	Inns there are none. Pretentious but
4079	Meagre, within a draughty hut,
4080	A bill of fare hangs full in sight
4081	And irritates the appetite.
4082	Meantime a Cyclops of those parts
4083	Before a fire which feebly glows
4084	Mends with the Russian hammer's blows
4085	The flimsy wares of Western marts,
4086	With blessings on the ditches and
4087	The ruts of his own fatherland.Yet on a frosty winter day
4088	The journey in a sledge doth please,
4089	No senseless fashionable lay
4090	Glides with a more luxurious ease;
4091	For our Automedons are fire
4092	And our swift troikas never tire;
4093	The verst posts catch the vacant eye
4094	And like a palisade flit by.
4095	The Larinas unwisely went,
4096	From apprehension of the cost,
4097	By their own horses, not the post--
4098	So Tania to her heart's content
4099	Could taste the pleasures of the road.
4100	Seven days and nights the travellers plod.
4101	But they draw near. Before them, lo!
4102	White Moscow raises her old spires,
4103	Whose countless golden crosses glow
4104	As with innumerable fires.
4105	Ah! brethren, what was my delight
4106	When I yon semicircle bright
4107	Of churches, gardens, belfries high
4108	Descried before me suddenly!
4109	Moscow, how oft in evil days,
4110	Condemned to exile dire by fate,
4111	On thee I used to meditate!
4112	Moscow! How much is in the phrase
4113	For every loyal Russian breast!
4114	How much is in that word expressed!
4115	Lo! compassed by his grove of oaks,
4116	Petrovski Palace! Gloomily
4117	His recent glory he invokes.
4118	Here, drunk with his late victory,
4119	Napoleon tarried till it please
4120	Moscow approach on bended knees,
4121	Time-honoured Kremlin's keys present.
4122	Not so! My Moscow never went
4123	To seek him out with bended head.
4124	No gift she bears, no feast proclaims,
4125	But lights incendiary flames
4126	For the impatient chief instead.
4127	From hence engrossed in thought profound
4128	He on the conflagration frowned.
4129	Adieu, thou witness of our glory,
4130	Petrovski Palace; come, astir!
4131	Drive on! the city barriers hoary
4132	Appear; along the road of Tver
4133	The coach is borne o'er ruts and holes,
4134	Past women, sentry-boxes, rolls,
4135	Past palaces and nunneries,
4136	Lamp-posts, shops, sledges, families,
4137	Bokharians, peasants, beds of greens,
4138	Boulevards, belfries, milliners,
4139	Huts, chemists, Cossacks, shopkeepers
4140	And fashionable magazines,
4141	Balconies, lion's heads on doors,
4142	Jackdaws on every spire--in scores.
4143	The weary way still incomplete,
4144	An hour passed by--another--till,
4145	Near Khariton's in a side street
4146	The coach before a house stood still.
4147	At an old aunt's they had arrived
4148	Who had for four long years survived
4149	An invalid from lung complaint.
4150	A Kalmuck gray, in caftan rent
4151	And spectacles, his knitting staid
4152	And the saloon threw open wide;
4153	The princess from the sofa cried
4154	And the newcomers welcome bade.
4155	The two old ladies then embraced
4156	And exclamations interlaced."Princesse, mon ange!"--"Pachette!"--
4157	"Aline!"
4158	"Who would have thought it? As of yore!
4159	Is it for long?"--"Ma chere cousine!"
4160	"Sit down. How funny, to be sure!
4161	'Tis a scene of romance, I vow!"
4162	"Tania, my eldest child, you know"--
4163	"Ah! come, Tattiana, come to me!
4164	Is it a dream, and can it be?
4165	Cousin, rememb'rest Grandison?"
4166	"What! Grandison?"--"Yes, certainly!"
4167	"Oh! I remember, where is he?"--
4168	"Here, he resides with Simeon.
4169	He called upon me Christmas Eve--
4170	His son is married, just conceive!""And he--but of him presently--
4171	To-morrow Tania we will show,
4172	What say you? to the family--
4173	Alas! abroad I cannot go.
4174	See, I can hardly crawl about--
4175	But you must both be quite tired out!
4176	Let us go seek a little rest--
4177	Ah! I'm so weak--my throbbing breast!
4178	Oppressive now is happiness,
4179	Not only sorrow--Ah! my dear,
4180	Now I am fit for nothing here.
4181	In old age life is weariness!"
4182	Then weeping she sank back distressed
4183	And fits of coughing racked her chest.By the sick lady's gaiety
4184	And kindness Tania was impressed,
4185	But, her own room in memory,
4186	The strange apartment her oppressed:
4187	Repose her silken curtains fled,
4188	She could not sleep in her new bed.
4189	The early tinkling of the bells
4190	Which of approaching labour tells
4191	Aroused Tattiana from her bed.
4192	The maiden at her casement sits
4193	As daylight glimmers, darkness flits,
4194	But ah! discerns nor wood nor mead--
4195	Beneath her lay a strange courtyard,
4196	A stable, kitchen, fence appeared.To consanguineous dinners they
4197	Conduct Tattiana constantly,
4198	That grandmothers and grandsires may
4199	Contemplate her sad reverie.
4200	We Russians, friends from distant parts
4201	Ever receive with kindly hearts
4202	And exclamations and good cheer.
4203	"How Tania grows! Doth it appear
4204	Long since I held thee at the font--
4205	Since in these arms I thee did bear--
4206	And since I pulled thee by the ear--
4207	And I to give thee cakes was wont?"--
4208	Then the old dames in chorus sing,
4209	"Oh! how our years are vanishing!"But nothing changed in them is seen,
4210	All in the good old style appears,
4211	Our dear old aunt, Princess Helene,
4212	Her cap of tulle still ever wears:
4213	Luceria Lvovna paint applies,
4214	Amy Petrovna  utters lies,
4215	Ivan Petrovitch still a gaby,
4216	Simeon Petrovitch just as shabby;
4217	Pelagie Nikolavna has
4218	Her friend Monsieur Finemouche the same,
4219	Her wolf-dog and her husband tame;
4220	Still of his club he member was--
4221	As deaf and silly doth remain,
4222	Still eats and drinks enough for twain.Their daughters kiss Tattiana fair.
4223	In the beginning, cold and mute,
4224	Moscow's young Graces at her stare,
4225	Examine her from head to foot.
4226	They deem her somewhat finical,
4227	Outlandish and provincial,
4228	A trifle pale, a trifle lean,
4229	But plainer girls they oft had seen.
4230	Obedient then to Nature's law,
4231	With her they did associate,
4232	Squeeze tiny hands and osculate;
4233	Her tresses curled in fashion saw,
4234	And oft in whispers would impart
4235	A maiden's secrets--of the heart.Triumphs--their own or those of friends--
4236	Hopes, frolics, dreams and sentiment
4237	Their harmless conversation blends
4238	With scandal's trivial ornament.
4239	Then to reward such confidence
4240	Her amorous experience
4241	With mute appeal to ask they seem--
4242	But Tania just as in a dream
4243	Without participation hears,
4244	Their voices nought to her impart
4245	And the lone secret of her heart,
4246	Her sacred hoard of joy and tears,
4247	She buries deep within her breast
4248	Nor aught confides unto the rest.Tattiana would have gladly heard
4249	The converse of the world polite,
4250	But in the drawing-room all appeared
4251	To find in gossip such delight,
4252	Speech was so tame and colourless
4253	Their slander e'en was weariness;
4254	In their sterility of prattle,
4255	Questions and news and tittle-tattle,
4256	No sense was ever manifest
4257	Though by an error and unsought--
4258	The languid mind could smile at nought,
4259	Heart would not throb albeit in jest--
4260	Even amusing fools we miss
4261	In thee, thou world of empty bliss.In groups, official striplings glance
4262	Conceitedly on Tania fair,
4263	And views amongst themselves advance
4264	Unfavourable unto her.
4265	But one buffoon unhappy deemed
4266	Her the ideal which he dreamed,
4267	And leaning 'gainst the portal closed
4268	To her an elegy composed.
4269	Also one Viazemski, remarking
4270	Tattiana by a poor aunt's side,
4271	Successfully to please her tried,
4272	And an old gent the poet marking
4273	By Tania, smoothing his peruke,
4274	To ask her name the trouble took.
4275	But where Melpomene doth rave
4276	With lengthened howl and accent loud,
4277	And her bespangled robe doth wave
4278	Before a cold indifferent crowd,
4279	And where Thalia softly dreams
4280	And heedless of approval seems,
4281	Terpsichore alone among
4282	Her sisterhood delights the young
4283	(So 'twas with us in former years,
4284	In your young days and also mine),
4285	Never upon my heroine
4286	The jealous dame her lorgnette veers,
4287	The connoisseur his glances throws
4288	From boxes or from stalls in rows.To the assembly her they bear.
4289	There the confusion, pressure, heat,
4290	The crash of music, candles' glare
4291	And rapid whirl of many feet,
4292	The ladies' dresses airy, light,
4293	The motley moving mass and bright,
4294	Young ladies in a vasty curve,
4295	To strike imagination serve.
4296	'Tis there that arrant fops display
4297	Their insolence and waistcoats white
4298	And glasses unemployed all night;
4299	Thither hussars on leave will stray
4300	To clank the spur, delight the fair--
4301	And vanish like a bird in air.Full many a lovely star hath night
4302	And Moscow many a beauty fair:
4303	Yet clearer shines than every light
4304	The moon in the blue atmosphere.
4305	And she to whom my lyre would fain,
4306	Yet dares not, dedicate its strain,
4307	Shines in the female firmament
4308	Like a full moon magnificent.
4309	Lo! with what pride celestial
4310	Her feet the earth beneath her press!
4311	Her heart how full of gentleness,
4312	Her glance how wild yet genial!
4313	Enough, enough, conclude thy lay--
4314	For folly's dues thou hadst to pay.Noise, laughter, bowing, hurrying mixt,
4315	Gallop, mazurka, waltzing--see!
4316	A pillar by, two aunts betwixt,
4317	Tania, observed by nobody,
4318	Looks upon all with absent gaze
4319	And hates the world's discordant ways.
4320	'Tis noisome to her there: in thought
4321	Again her rural life she sought,
4322	The hamlet, the poor villagers,
4323	The little solitary nook
4324	Where shining runs the tiny brook,
4325	Her garden, and those books of hers,
4326	And the lime alley's twilight dim
4327	Where the first time she met with _him_.Thus widely meditation erred,
4328	Forgot the world, the noisy ball,
4329	Whilst from her countenance ne'er stirred
4330	The eyes of a grave general.
4331	Both aunts looked knowing as a judge,
4332	Each gave Tattiana's arm a nudge
4333	And in a whisper did repeat:
4334	"Look quickly to your left, my sweet!"
4335	"The left? Why, what on earth is there?"--
4336	"No matter, look immediately.
4337	There, in that knot of company,
4338	Two dressed in uniform appear--
4339	Ah! he has gone the other way"--
4340	"Who? Is it that stout general, pray?"--Let us congratulations pay
4341	To our Tattiana conquering,
4342	And for a time our course delay,
4343	That I forget not whom I sing.
4344	Let me explain that in my song
4345	"I celebrate a comrade young
4346	And the extent of his caprice;
4347	O epic Muse, my powers increase
4348	And grant success to labour long;
4349	Having a trusty staff bestowed,
4350	Grant that I err not on the road."
4351	Enough! my pack is now unslung--
4352	To classicism I've homage paid,
4353	Though late, have a beginning made.
4354	The Great World
4355	'Fare thee well, and if for ever,
4356	Still for ever fare thee well.'--Byron
4357	In the Lyceum's noiseless shade
4358	As in a garden when I grew,
4359	I Apuleius gladly read
4360	But would not look at Cicero.
4361	'Twas then in valleys lone, remote,
4362	In spring-time, heard the cygnet's note
4363	By waters shining tranquilly,
4364	That first the Muse appeared to me.
4365	Into the study of the boy
4366	There came a sudden flash of light,
4367	The Muse revealed her first delight,
4368	Sang childhood's pastimes and its joy,
4369	Glory with which our history teems
4370	And the heart's agitated dreams.
4371	And the world met her smilingly,
4372	A first success light pinions gave,
4373	The old Derjavine noticed me,
4374	And blest me, sinking to the grave.
4375	Then my companions young with pleasure
4376	In the unfettered hours of leisure
4377	Her utterances ever heard,
4378	And by a partial temper stirred
4379	And boiling o'er with friendly heat,
4380	They first of all my brow did wreathe
4381	And an encouragement did breathe
4382	That my coy Muse might sing more sweet.
4383	O triumphs of my guileless days,
4384	How sweet a dream your memories raise!
4385	Passion's wild sway I then allowed,
4386	Her promptings unto law did make,
4387	Pursuits I followed of the crowd,
4388	My sportive Muse I used to take
4389	To many a noisy feast and fight,
4390	Terror of guardians of the night;
4391	And wild festivities among
4392	She brought with her the gift of song.
4393	Like a Bacchante in her sport
4394	Beside the cup she sang her rhymes
4395	And the young revellers of past times
4396	Vociferously paid her court,
4397	And I, amid the friendly crowd,
4398	Of my light paramour was proud.
4399	But I abandoned their array,
4400	And fled afar--she followed me.
4401	How oft the kindly Muse away
4402	Hath whiled the road's monotony,
4403	Entranced me by some mystic tale.
4404	How oft beneath the moonbeams pale
4405	Like Leonora did she ride
4406	With me Caucasian rocks beside!
4407	How oft to the Crimean shore
4408	She led me through nocturnal mist
4409	Unto the sounding sea to list,
4410	Where Nereids murmur evermore,
4411	And where the billows hoarsely raise
4412	To God eternal hymns of praise.
4413	Then, the far capital forgot,
4414	Its splendour and its blandishments,
4415	In poor Moldavia cast her lot,
4416	She visited the humble tents
4417	Of migratory gipsy hordes--
4418	And wild among them grew her words--
4419	Our godlike tongue she could exchange
4420	For savage speech, uncouth and strange,
4421	And ditties of the steppe she loved.
4422	But suddenly all changed around!
4423	Lo! in my garden was she found
4424	And as a country damsel roved,
4425	A pensive sorrow in her glance
4426	And in her hand a French romance.
4427	Now for the first time I my Muse
4428	Lead into good society,
4429	Her steppe-like beauties I peruse
4430	With jealous fear, anxiety.
4431	Through dense aristocratic rows
4432	Of diplomats and warlike beaux
4433	And supercilious dames she glides,
4434	Sits down and gazes on all sides--
4435	Amazed at the confusing crowd,
4436	Variety of speech and vests,
4437	Deliberate approach of guests
4438	Who to the youthful hostess bowed,
4439	And the dark fringe of men, like frames
4440	Enclosing pictures of fair dames.
4441	Assemblies oligarchical
4442	Please her by their decorum fixed,
4443	The rigour of cold pride and all
4444	Titles and ages intermixed.
4445	But who in that choice company
4446	With clouded brow stands silently?
4447	Unknown to all he doth appear,
4448	A vision desolate and drear
4449	Doth seem to him the festal scene.
4450	Doth his brow wretchedness declare
4451	Or suffering pride? Why is he there?
4452	Who may he be? Is it Eugene?
4453	Pray is it he? It is the same.
4454	"And is it long since back he came?
4455	"Is he the same or grown more wise?
4456	Still doth the misanthrope appear?
4457	He has returned, say in what guise?
4458	What is his latest character?
4459	What doth he act? Is it Melmoth,
4460	Philanthropist or patriot,
4461	Childe Harold, quaker, devotee,
4462	Or other mask donned playfully?
4463	Or a good fellow for the nonce,
4464	Like you and me and all the rest?--
4465	But this is my advice, 'twere best
4466	Not to behave as he did once--
4467	Society he duped enow."
4468	"Is he known to you?"--"Yes and No."Wherefore regarding him express
4469	Perverse, unfavourable views?
4470	Is it that human restlessness
4471	For ever carps, condemns, pursues?
4472	Is it that ardent souls of flame
4473	By recklessness amuse or shame
4474	Selfish nonentities around?
4475	That mind which yearns for space is bound?
4476	And that too often we receive
4477	Professions eagerly for deeds,
4478	That crass stupidity misleads,
4479	That we by cant ourselves deceive,
4480	That mediocrity alone
4481	Without disgust we look upon?Happy he who in youth was young,
4482	Happy who timely grew mature,
4483	He who life's frosts which early wrung
4484	Hath gradually learnt to endure;
4485	By visions who was ne'er deranged
4486	Nor from the mob polite estranged,
4487	At twenty who was prig or swell,
4488	At thirty who was married well,
4489	At fifty who relief obtained
4490	From public and from private ties,
4491	Who glory, wealth and dignities
4492	Hath tranquilly in turn attained,
4493	And unto whom we all allude
4494	As to a worthy man and good!But sad is the reflection made,
4495	In vain was youth by us received,
4496	That we her constantly betrayed
4497	And she at last hath us deceived;
4498	That our desires which noblest seemed,
4499	The purest of the dreams we dreamed,
4500	Have one by one all withered grown
4501	Like rotten leaves by Autumn strown--
4502	'Tis fearful to anticipate
4503	Nought but of dinners a long row,
4504	To look on life as on a show,
4505	Eternally to imitate
4506	The seemly crowd, partaking nought
4507	Its passions and its modes of thought.The butt of scandal having been,
4508	'Tis dreadful--ye agree, I hope--
4509	To pass with reasonable men
4510	For a fictitious misanthrope,
4511	A visionary mortified,
4512	Or monster of Satanic pride,
4513	Or e'en the "Demon" of my strain.
4514	Oneguine--take him up again--
4515	In duel having killed his friend
4516	And reached, with nought his mind to engage,
4517	The twenty-sixth year of his age,
4518	Wearied of leisure in the end,
4519	Without profession, business, wife,
4520	He knew not how to spend his life.
4521	Him a disquietude did seize,
4522	A wish from place to place to roam,
4523	A very troublesome disease,
4524	In some a willing martyrdom.
4525	Abandoned he his country seat,
4526	Of woods and fields the calm retreat,
4527	Where every day before his eyes
4528	A blood-bespattered shade would rise,
4529	And aimless journeys did commence--
4530	But still remembrance to him clings,
4531	His travels like all other things
4532	Inspired but weariness intense;
4533	Returning, from his ship amid
4534	A ball he fell as Tchatzki did.
4535	Behold, the crowd begins to stir,
4536	A whisper runs along the hall,
4537	A lady draws the hostess near,
4538	Behind her a grave general.
4539	Her manners were deliberate,
4540	Reserved, but not inanimate,
4541	Her eyes no saucy glance address,
4542	There was no angling for success.
4543	Her features no grimaces bleared;
4544	Of affectation innocent,
4545	Calm and without embarrassment,
4546	A faithful model she appeared
4547	Of "comme il faut." Shishkoff, forgive!
4548	I can't translate the adjective.
4549	Ladies in crowds around her close,
4550	Her with a smile old women greet,
4551	The men salute with lower bows
4552	And watch her eye's full glance to meet.
4553	Maidens before her meekly move
4554	Along the hall, and high above
4555	The crowd doth head and shoulders rise
4556	The general who accompanies.
4557	None could her beautiful declare,
4558	Yet viewing her from head to foot,
4559	None could a trace of that impute,
4560	Which in the elevated sphere
4561	Of London life is "vulgar" called
4562	And ruthless fashion hath blackballed.I like this word exceedingly
4563	Although it will not bear translation,
4564	With us 'tis quite a novelty
4565	Not high in general estimation;
4566	'Twould serve ye in an epigram--
4567	But turn we once more to our dame.
4568	Enchanting, but unwittingly,
4569	At table she was sitting by
4570	The brilliant Nina Voronskoi,
4571	The Neva's Cleopatra, and
4572	None the conviction could withstand
4573	That Nina's marble symmetry,
4574	Though dazzling its effulgence white,
4575	Could not eclipse her neighbour's light."And is it," meditates Eugene.
4576	"And is it she? It must be--no--
4577	How! from the waste of steppes unseen,"--
4578	And the eternal lorgnette through
4579	Frequent and rapid doth his glance
4580	Seek the forgotten countenance
4581	Familiar to him long ago.
4582	"Inform me, prince, pray dost thou know
4583	The lady in the crimson cap
4584	Who with the Spanish envoy speaks?"--
4585	The prince's eye Oneguine seeks:
4586	"Ah! long the world hath missed thy shape!
4587	But stop! I will present thee, if
4588	You choose."--"But who is she?"--"My wife.""So thou art wed! I did not know.
4589	Long ago?"--"'Tis the second year."
4590	"To--?"--"Larina."--"Tattiana?"--"So.
4591	And dost thou know her?"--"We live near."
4592	"Then come with me." The prince proceeds,
4593	His wife approaches, with him leads
4594	His relative and friend as well.
4595	The lady's glance upon him fell--
4596	And though her soul might be confused,
4597	And vehemently though amazed
4598	She on the apparition gazed,
4599	No signs of trouble her accused,
4600	A mien unaltered she preserved,
4601	Her bow was easy, unreserved.Ah no! no faintness her attacked
4602	Nor sudden turned she red or white,
4603	Her brow she did not e'en contract
4604	Nor yet her lip compressed did bite.
4605	Though he surveyed her at his ease,
4606	Not the least trace Oneguine sees
4607	Of the Tattiana of times fled.
4608	He conversation would have led--
4609	But could not. Then she questioned him:--
4610	"Had he been long here, and where from?
4611	Straight from their province had he come?"--
4612	Cast upwards then her eyeballs dim
4613	Unto her husband, went away--
4614	Transfixed Oneguine mine doth stay.Is this the same Tattiana, say,
4615	Before whom once in solitude,
4616	In the beginning of this lay,
4617	Deep in the distant province rude,
4618	Impelled by zeal for moral worth,
4619	He salutary rules poured forth?
4620	The maid whose note he still possessed
4621	Wherein the heart its vows expressed,
4622	Where all upon the surface lies,--
4623	That girl--but he must dreaming be--
4624	That girl whom once on a time he
4625	Could in a humble sphere despise,
4626	Can she have been a moment gone
4627	Thus haughty, careless in her tone?He quits the fashionable throng
4628	And meditative homeward goes,
4629	Visions, now sad, now grateful, long
4630	Do agitate his late repose.
4631	He wakes--they with a letter come--
4632	The Princess N. will be at home
4633	On such a day. O Heavens, 'tis she!
4634	Oh! I accept. And instantly
4635	He a polite reply doth scrawl.
4636	What hath he dreamed? What hath occurred?
4637	In the recesses what hath stirred
4638	Of a heart cold and cynical?
4639	Vexation? Vanity? or strove
4640	Again the plague of boyhood--love?The hours once more Oneguine counts,
4641	Impatient waits the close of day,
4642	But ten strikes and his sledge he mounts
4643	And gallops to her house away.
4644	Trembling he seeks the young princess--
4645	Tattiana finds in loneliness.
4646	Together moments one or two
4647	They sat, but conversation's flow
4648	Deserted Eugene. He, distraught,
4649	Sits by her gloomily, desponds,
4650	Scarce to her questions he responds,
4651	Full of exasperating thought.
4652	He fixedly upon her stares--
4653	She calm and unconcerned appears.The husband comes and interferes
4654	With this unpleasant _tete-a-tete_,
4655	With Eugene pranks of former years
4656	And jests doth recapitulate.
4657	They talked and laughed. The guests arrived.
4658	The conversation was revived
4659	By the coarse wit of worldly hate;
4660	But round the hostess scintillate
4661	Light sallies without coxcombry,
4662	Awhile sound conversation seems
4663	To banish far unworthy themes
4664	And platitudes and pedantry,
4665	And never was the ear affright
4666	By liberties or loose or light.And yet the city's flower was there,
4667	Noblesse and models of the mode,
4668	Faces which we meet everywhere
4669	And necessary fools allowed.
4670	Behold the dames who once were fine
4671	With roses, caps and looks malign;
4672	Some marriageable maids behold,
4673	Blank, unapproachable and cold.
4674	Lo, the ambassador who speaks
4675	Economy political,
4676	And with gray hair ambrosial
4677	The old man who has had his freaks,
4678	Renowned for his acumen, wit,
4679	But now ridiculous a bit.Behold Sabouroff, whom the age
4680	For baseness of the spirit scorns,
4681	Saint Priest, who every album's page
4682	With blunted pencil-point adorns.
4683	Another tribune of the ball
4684	Hung like a print against the wall,
4685	Pink as Palm Sunday cherubim,
4686	Motionless, mute, tight-laced and trim.
4687	The traveller, bird of passage he,
4688	Stiff, overstarched and insolent,
4689	Awakens secret merriment
4690	By his embarrassed dignity--
4691	Mute glances interchanged aside
4692	Meet punishment for him provide.
4693	But my Oneguine the whole eve
4694	Within his mind Tattiana bore,
4695	Not the young timid maid, believe,
4696	Enamoured, simple-minded, poor,
4697	But the indifferent princess,
4698	Divinity without access
4699	Of the imperial Neva's shore.
4700	O Men, how very like ye are
4701	To Eve the universal mother,
4702	Possession hath no power to please,
4703	The serpent to unlawful trees
4704	Aye bids ye in some way or other--
4705	Unless forbidden fruit we eat,
4706	Our paradise is no more sweet.Ah! how Tattiana was transformed,
4707	How thoroughly her part she took!
4708	How soon to habits she conformed
4709	Which crushing dignity must brook!
4710	Who would the maiden innocent
4711	In the unmoved, magnificent
4712	Autocrat of the drawing-room seek?
4713	And he had made her heart beat quick!
4714	'Twas he whom, amid nightly shades,
4715	Whilst Morpheus his approach delays,
4716	She mourned and to the moon would raise
4717	The languid eye of love-sick maids,
4718	Dreaming perchance in weal or woe
4719	To end with him her path below.To Love all ages lowly bend,
4720	But the young unpolluted heart
4721	His gusts should fertilize, amend,
4722	As vernal storms the fields athwart.
4723	Youth freshens beneath Passion's showers,
4724	Develops and matures its powers,
4725	And thus in season the rich field
4726	Gay flowers and luscious fruit doth yield.
4727	But at a later, sterile age,
4728	The solstice of our earthly years,
4729	Mournful Love's deadly trace appears
4730	As storms which in chill autumn rage
4731	And leave a marsh the fertile ground
4732	And devastate the woods around.There was no doubt! Eugene, alas!
4733	Tattiana loved as when a lad,
4734	Both day and night he now must pass
4735	In love-lorn meditation sad.
4736	Careless of every social rule,
4737	The crystals of her vestibule
4738	He daily in his drives drew near
4739	And like a shadow haunted her.
4740	Enraptured was he if allowed
4741	To swathe her shoulders in the furs,
4742	If his hot hand encountered hers,
4743	Or he dispersed the motley crowd
4744	Of lackeys in her pathway grouped,
4745	Or to pick up her kerchief stooped.She seemed of him oblivious,
4746	Despite the anguish of his breast,
4747	Received him freely at her house,
4748	At times three words to him addressed
4749	In company, or simply bowed,
4750	Or recognized not in the crowd.
4751	No coquetry was there, I vouch--
4752	Society endures not such!
4753	Oneguine's cheek grew ashy pale,
4754	Either she saw not or ignored;
4755	Oneguine wasted; on my word,
4756	Already he grew phthisical.
4757	All to the doctors Eugene send,
4758	And they the waters recommend.He went not--sooner was prepared
4759	To write his forefathers to warn
4760	Of his approach; but nothing cared
4761	Tattiana--thus the sex is born.--
4762	He obstinately will remain,
4763	Still hopes, endeavours, though in vain.
4764	Sickness more courage doth command
4765	Than health, so with a trembling hand
4766	A love epistle he doth scrawl.
4767	Though correspondence as a rule
4768	He used to hate--and was no fool--
4769	Yet suffering emotional
4770	Had rendered him an invalid;
4771	But word for word his letter read.All is foreseen. My secret drear
4772	Will sound an insult in your ear.
4773	What acrimonious scorn I trace
4774	Depicted on your haughty face!
4775	What do I ask? What cause assigned
4776	That I to you reveal my mind?
4777	To what malicious merriment,
4778	It may be, I yield nutriment!
4779	Meeting you in times past by chance,
4780	Warmth I imagined in your glance,
4781	But, knowing not the actual truth,
4782	Restrained the impulses of youth;
4783	Also my wretched liberty
4784	I would not part with finally;
4785	This separated us as well--
4786	Lenski, unhappy victim, fell,
4787	From everything the heart held dear
4788	I then resolved my heart to tear;
4789	Unknown to all, without a tie,
4790	I thought--retirement, liberty,
4791	Will happiness replace. My God!
4792	How I have erred and felt the rod!
4793	No, ever to behold your face,
4794	To follow you in every place,
4795	Your smiling lips, your beaming eyes,
4796	To watch with lovers' ecstasies,
4797	Long listen, comprehend the whole
4798	Of your perfections in my soul,
4799	Before you agonized to die--
4800	This, this were true felicity!
4801	But such is not for me. I brood
4802	Daily of love in solitude.
4803	My days of life approach their end,
4804	Yet I in idleness expend
4805	The remnant destiny concedes,
4806	And thus each stubbornly proceeds.
4807	I feel, allotted is my span;
4808	But, that life longer may remain,
4809	At morn I must assuredly
4810	Know that thy face that day I see.
4811	I tremble lest my humble prayer
4812	You with stern countenance declare
4813	The artifice of villany--
4814	I hear your harsh, reproachful cry.
4815	If ye but knew how dreadful 'tis
4816	To bear love's parching agonies--
4817	To burn, yet reason keep awake
4818	The fever of the blood to slake--
4819	A passionate desire to bend
4820	And, sobbing at your feet, to blend
4821	Entreaties, woes and prayers, confess
4822	All that the heart would fain express--
4823	Yet with a feigned frigidity
4824	To arm the tongue and e'en the eye,
4825	To be in conversation clear
4826	And happy unto you appear.
4827	So be it! But internal strife
4828	I cannot longer wage concealed.
4829	The die is cast! Thine is my life!
4830	Into thy hands my fate I yield!No answer! He another sent.
4831	Epistle second, note the third,
4832	Remained unnoticed. Once he went
4833	To an assembly--she appeared
4834	Just as he entered. How severe!
4835	She will not see, she will not hear.
4836	Alas! she is as hard, behold,
4837	And frosty as a Twelfth Night cold.
4838	Oh, how her lips compressed restrain
4839	The indignation of her heart!
4840	A sidelong look doth Eugene dart:
4841	Where, where, remorse, compassion, pain?
4842	Where, where, the trace of tears? None, none!
4843	Upon her brow sits wrath alone--And it may be a secret dread
4844	Lest the world or her lord divine
4845	A certain little escapade
4846	Well known unto Oneguine mine.
4847	'Tis hopeless! Homeward doth he flee
4848	Cursing his own stupidity,
4849	And brooding o'er the ills he bore,
4850	Society renounced once more.
4851	Then in the silent cabinet
4852	He in imagination saw
4853	The time when Melancholy's claw
4854	'Mid worldly pleasures chased him yet,
4855	Caught him and by the collar took
4856	And shut him in a lonely nook.He read as vainly as before,
4857	Perusing Gibbon and Rousseau,
4858	Manzoni, Herder and Chamfort,
4859	Madame de Stael, Bichat, Tissot:
4860	He read the unbelieving Bayle,
4861	Also the works of Fontenelle,
4862	Some Russian authors he perused--
4863	Nought in the universe refused:
4864	Nor almanacs nor newspapers,
4865	Which lessons unto us repeat,
4866	Wherein I castigation get;
4867	And where a madrigal occurs
4868	Writ in my honour now and then--
4869	_E sempre bene_, gentlemen!
4870	But what results? His eyes peruse
4871	But thoughts meander far away--
4872	Ideas, desires and woes confuse
4873	His intellect in close array.
4874	His eyes, the printed lines betwixt,
4875	On lines invisible are fixt;
4876	'Twas these he read and these alone
4877	His spirit was intent upon.
4878	They were the wonderful traditions
4879	Of kindly, dim antiquity,
4880	Dreams with no continuity,
4881	Prophecies, threats and apparitions,
4882	The lively trash of stories long
4883	Or letters of a maiden young.And by degrees upon him grew
4884	A lethargy of sense, a trance,
4885	And soon imagination threw
4886	Before him her wild game of chance.
4887	And now upon the snow in thaw
4888	A young man motionless he saw,
4889	As one who bivouacs afield,
4890	And heard a voice cry--_Why! He's killed!_--
4891	And now he views forgotten foes,
4892	Poltroons and men of slanderous tongue,
4893	Bevies of treacherous maidens young;
4894	Of thankless friends the circle rose,
4895	A mansion--by the window, see!
4896	She sits alone--'tis ever _she!_So frequently his mind would stray
4897	He well-nigh lost the use of sense,
4898	Almost became a poet say--
4899	Oh! what had been his eminence!
4900	Indeed, by force of magnetism
4901	A Russian poem's mechanism
4902	My scholar without aptitude
4903	At this time almost understood.
4904	How like a poet was my chum
4905	When, sitting by his fire alone
4906	Whilst cheerily the embers shone,
4907	He "Benedetta" used to hum,
4908	Or "Idol mio," and in the grate
4909	Would lose his slippers or gazette.Time flies! a genial air abroad,
4910	Winter resigned her empire white,
4911	Oneguine ne'er as poet showed
4912	Nor died nor lost his senses quite.
4913	Spring cheered him up, and he resigned
4914	His chambers close wherein confined
4915	He marmot-like did hibernate,
4916	His double sashes and his grate,
4917	And sallied forth one brilliant morn--
4918	Along the Neva's bank he sleighs,
4919	On the blue blocks of ice the rays
4920	Of the sun glisten; muddy, worn,
4921	The snow upon the streets doth melt--
4922	Whither along them doth he pelt?Oneguine whither gallops? Ye
4923	Have guessed already. Yes, quite so!
4924	Unto his own Tattiana he,
4925	Incorrigible rogue, doth go.
4926	Her house he enters, ghastly white,
4927	The vestibule finds empty quite--
4928	He enters the saloon. 'Tis blank!
4929	A door he opens. But why shrank
4930	He back as from a sudden blow?--
4931	Alone the princess sitteth there,
4932	Pallid and with dishevelled hair,
4933	Gazing upon a note below.
4934	Her tears flow plentifully and
4935	Her cheek reclines upon her hand.Oh! who her speechless agonies
4936	Could not in that brief moment guess!
4937	Who now could fail to recognize
4938	Tattiana in the young princess!
4939	Tortured by pangs of wild regret,
4940	Eugene fell prostrate at her feet--
4941	She starts, nor doth a word express,
4942	But gazes on Oneguine's face
4943	Without amaze or wrath displayed:
4944	His sunken eye and aspect faint,
4945	Imploring looks and mute complaint
4946	She comprehends. The simple maid
4947	By fond illusions once possest
4948	Is once again made manifest.
4949	His kneeling posture he retains--
4950	Calmly her eyes encounter his--
4951	Insensible her hand remains
4952	Beneath his lips' devouring kiss.
4953	What visions then her fancy thronged--
4954	A breathless silence then, prolonged--
4955	But finally she softly said:
4956	"Enough, arise! for much we need
4957	Without disguise ourselves explain.
4958	Oneguine, hast forgotten yet
4959	The hour when--Fate so willed--we met
4960	In the lone garden and the lane?
4961	How meekly then I heard you preach--
4962	To-day it is my turn to teach.
4963	"Oneguine, I was younger then,
4964	And better, if I judge aright;
4965	I loved you--what did I obtain?
4966	Affection how did you requite?
4967	But with austerity!--for you
4968	No novelty--is it not true?--
4969	Was the meek love a maiden feels.
4970	But now--my very blood congeals,
4971	Calling to mind your icy look
4972	And sermon--but in that dread hour
4973	I blame not your behaviour--
4974	An honourable course ye took,
4975	Displayed a noble rectitude--
4976	My soul is filled with gratitude!
4977	"Then, in the country, is't not true?
4978	And far removed from rumour vain;
4979	I did not please you. Why pursue
4980	Me now, inflict upon me pain?--
4981	Wherefore am I your quarry held?--
4982	Is it that I am now compelled
4983	To move in fashionable life,
4984	That I am rich, a prince's wife?--
4985	Because my lord, in battles maimed,
4986	Is petted by the Emperor?--
4987	That my dishonour would ensure
4988	A notoriety proclaimed,
4989	And in society might shed
4990	A bastard fame prohibited?
4991	"I weep. And if within your breast
4992	My image hath not disappeared,
4993	Know that your sarcasm ill-suppressed,
4994	Your conversation cold and hard,
4995	If the choice in my power were,
4996	To lawless love I should prefer--
4997	And to these letters and these tears.
4998	For visions of my childish years
4999	Then ye were barely generous,
5000	Age immature averse to cheat--
5001	But now--what brings you to my feet?--
5002	How mean, how pusillanimous!
5003	A prudent man like you and brave
5004	To shallow sentiment a slave!
5005	"Oneguine, all this sumptuousness,
5006	The gilding of life's vanities,
5007	In the world's vortex my success,
5008	My splendid house and gaieties--
5009	What are they? Gladly would I yield
5010	This life in masquerade concealed,
5011	This glitter, riot, emptiness,
5012	For my wild garden and bookcase,--
5013	Yes! for our unpretending home,
5014	Oneguine--the beloved place
5015	Where the first time I saw your face,--
5016	Or for the solitary tomb
5017	Wherein my poor old nurse doth lie
5018	Beneath a cross and shrubbery.
5019	"'Twas possible then, happiness--
5020	Nay, near--but destiny decreed--
5021	My lot is fixed--with thoughtlessness
5022	It may be that I did proceed--
5023	With bitter tears my mother prayed,
5024	And for Tattiana, mournful maid,
5025	Indifferent was her future fate.
5026	I married--now, I supplicate--
5027	For ever your Tattiana leave.
5028	Your heart possesses, I know well,
5029	Honour and pride inflexible.
5030	I love you--to what end deceive?--
5031	But I am now another's bride--
5032	For ever faithful will abide."
5033	She rose--departed. But Eugene
5034	Stood as if struck by lightning fire.
5035	What a storm of emotions keen
5036	Raged round him and of balked desire!
5037	And hark! the clank of spurs is heard
5038	And Tania's husband soon appeared.--
5039	But now our hero we must leave
5040	Just at a moment which I grieve
5041	Must be pronounced unfortunate--
5042	For long--for ever. To be sure
5043	Together we have wandered o'er
5044	The world enough. Congratulate
5045	Each other as the shore we climb!
5046	Hurrah! it long ago was time!
5047	Reader, whoever thou mayst be,
5048	Foeman or friend, I do aspire
5049	To part in amity with thee!
5050	Adieu! whate'er thou didst desire
5051	From careless stanzas such as these,
5052	Of passion reminiscences,
5053	Pictures of the amusing scene,
5054	Repose from labour, satire keen,
5055	Or faults of grammar on its page--
5056	God grant that all who herein glance,
5057	In serious mood or dalliance
5058	Or in a squabble to engage,
5059	May find a crumb to satisfy.
5060	Now we must separate. Good-bye!
5061	And farewell thou, my gloomy friend,
5062	Thou also, my ideal true,
5063	And thou, persistent to the end,
5064	My little book. With thee I knew
5065	All that a poet could desire,
5066	Oblivion of life's tempest dire,
5067	Of friends the grateful intercourse--
5068	Oh, many a year hath run its course
5069	Since I beheld Eugene and young
5070	Tattiana in a misty dream,
5071	And my romance's open theme
5072	Glittered in a perspective long,
5073	And I discerned through Fancy's prism
5074	Distinctly not its mechanism.
5075	But ye to whom, when friendship heard,
5076	The first-fruits of my tale I read,
5077	As Saadi anciently averred--
5078	Some are afar and some are dead.
5079	Without them Eugene is complete;
5080	And thou, from whom Tattiana sweet;
5081	Was drawn, ideal of my lay--
5082	Ah! what hath fate not torn away!
5083	Happy who quit life's banquet seat
5084	Before the dregs they shall divine
5085	Of the cup brimming o'er with wine--
5086	Who the romance do not complete,
5087	But who abandon it--as I
5088	Have my Oneguine--suddenly.
